Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Testimony Must Match Claim and Witnesses Must Agree
Rulings on acceptance of testimony and required agreement between witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that testimony must agree with the claim and witnesses must agree in wording and meaning, and apply it to cases where witnesses give different amounts, including the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Testimony is accepted only if it agrees with the claim and witnesses agree in wording and meaning; if they differ, the lower common amount may be accepted (Sahibayn view).

This lesson examines a fundamental principle of Hanafi testimony law: the requirement that testimony must match the claim (da'wa) and that two witnesses must be concordant in both wording (lafz) and meaning (ma'na). We will see how al-Quduri presents this rule and then handles a classic dispute when witnesses give differing amounts. Understanding this principle is essential for any legal practitioner—it ensures that testimony reliably supports the plaintiff's case and avoids contradictions that undermine credibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fundamental rule
The passage begins with a clear condition: testimony is accepted only if it agrees with the claim (da'wa). If it contradicts the claim, it is rejected.
This ensures that testimony directly supports the case.
2
State the requirement of witness concordance
The text then introduces a second condition: the two witnesses must agree in wording (lafz) and meaning (ma'na). This is critical for the validity of their testimony.
Hanafis are stricter than some other schools in requiring exact wording agreement.
3
Apply the rule to the case of differing amounts
If one witness says 1000 and the other says 2000, there is a clear difference in meaning. According to Abu Hanifa, the testimony is not accepted because the witnesses do not agree. According to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), they agree on the existence of at least 1000, so testimony is accepted for that amount.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with practical consequences.
4
Analyze the evidence for each position
Abu Hanifa relies on the strict requirement of agreement. The Sahibayn point to the common element: both affirm a debt of at least 1000. Their approach is supported by the practice of Shuraih and other early authorities.
The Quranic verse (2:282) provides the general basis for testimony but does not specify the rule for disagreement.
5
Determine the operative ruling for fatwa
Later Hanafi authorities, including those in al-Hidayah and the later maslak, have preferred the Sahibayn's view for practical reasons. Therefore, the mufta bihi is to accept the lower amount when witnesses differ on the quantum.
This illustrates how tarjih works within the Hanafi school: the later jumhur opt for the more workable position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الشَّهَادَاتِ
وَإِذَا وَافَقَتْ الشَّهَادَةُ الدَّعْوَى قُبِلَتْ وَإِنْ خَالَفَتْهَا لَمْ تُقْبَل ٣٣ وَيُعْتَبَرُ اتِّفَاقُ الشَّاهِدَيْنِ فِي اللَّفْظِ وَالْمَعْنَى فَإِنْ شَهِدَ أَحَدُهُمَا بِأَلْفِ وَالآخَرُ بِأَلْفَيْنِ لَمْ تُقْبَلْ شَهَادَتُهُمَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ: تُقْبَلُ بِالْأَلْفِ فَإِنْ شَهِدَ أَحَدُهُمَا بِأَلْفِ وَالآخَرُ بِأَلْفِ وَخَمْسِمِائَةٍ وَالْمُدَّعِي يَدَّعِي أَلْفًا وَخَمْسَمِائَةِ قُبِلَتْ الشَّهَادَةُ بِأَلْفِ
وَإِذَا شَهِدَ بِأَلْفِ وَقَالَ آخَرُ: قَضَاهُ مِنْهَا خَمْسَمِائَةٍ قُبِلَتْ شَهَادَتُهُ بِأَلْفِ وَلَمْ يُقْبَلْ قَوْلُهُ إِلَّا أَنْ يَشْهَدَ مَعَهُ آخَرُ ٣٢ وَيَنْبَغِي لِلشَّاهِدِ إِذَا عَلِمَ ذَلِكَ أَنْ لَا يَشْهَدَ بِأَلْفِ حَتَّى يُقِرَّ الْمُدَّعِي أَنَّهُ قَبَضَ خَمْسَمِائَةٍ
٣٥ وَإِذَا شَهِدَ شَاهِدَانِ أَنَّ زَيْدًا قُتِلَ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ بِمَكَّةَ وَشَهِدَ آخَرَانِ أَنَّهُ قُتِلَ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ بِالْكُوفَةِ وَاجْتَمَعُوا عِنْدَ الْحَاكِمِ لَمْ يَقْبَلُ الشَّهَادَتَيْنِ
وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَتُقْبَلُ شَهَادَةُ الْأَقْلَفَ اقَدْ مَضَى فِي حَدِيثِ أَنَسِ بْنِ مَالِكِ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ قَالَ: الْمُؤْمِنُونَ شُهَدَاءُ اللهِ فِي الْأَرْضِ ، وَرُوِّينَا عَنْ عَطَاءِ وَالشَّعْيَ أَنَّهُمَا قَالَا: " تَجُوزُ شَهَادَةً
ولد الزنا ( الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ : شَهَادَةُ وَلَدِ الزَّنَا ، نمبر 21180 مصنف عبد الرزاق، ، 15381) وجه (۱) دلیل امام مالک الحدیث لثبوت وَتُقْبَلُ شَهَادَةُ الْأَقْلَفِ اعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ ، قَالَ:
قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : «وَلَدُ الزِّنَا شَرُّ الثَّلَاثَةِ»، المستدرك علي الصحيحين، للحاكم، نمبر 2853) ۳۲. وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَيُعْتَبَرُ اتَّفَاقُ الشَّاهِدَيْنِ فِي اللَّفْظِ وَالْمَعْنَى \ عَنْ شُرَيْحٍ، فِي شَاهِدَيْنِ يَخْتَلِفَانِ فَشَهِدَ أَحَدُهُمَا عَلَى عِشْرِينَ وَالْآخَرُ عَلَى عَشْرَةٍ قَالَ: «يُؤْخَذُ بِالْعَشَرَةِ»، (»، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في الشَّاهِدَيْنِ يَخْتَلِفَانِ، غبر 20718) ٣٣ وجه: (ا) الآية لثبوت وَإِذَا شَهِدَ بِأَلْفِ وَقَالَ آخَرُ : ﴿وَاسْتَشْهِدُواْ شَهِيدَيْنِ مِن رِجَالِكُمْ فَإِن لَّمْ يَكُونَا رَجُلَيْنِ فَرَجُلٌ وَامْرَأَتَانِ مِمَّن تَرْضَوْنَ مِنَ الشُّهَدَاءِ أَن تَضِلَّ إِحْدَيْهُمَا فَتُذَكَّرَ إِحْدَنَهُمَا الْأُخْرَى) (سورة البقرة، 2 أيت، نمبر 282)
٣٥وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِذَا شَهِدَ شَاهِدَانِ أَنَّ زَيْدًا قُتِلَ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِمَكَةَ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ فِي اصول: دونوں گواہ لفظ و معنی کے اعتبار سے موافق ہو تو گواہی قبول کی جائے گی امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک۔ اصول: گواہ نے پندرہ سو کی گواہی دی اور مدعی نے ایک ہزار کا اقرار کیا گواہی غیر مقبول ہو گی۔
The Book of Testimonies. If the testimony agrees with the claim, it is accepted; if it contradicts, it is not accepted. Consideration is given to the agreement of the two witnesses in wording and meaning. If one testifies to one thousand and the other to two thousand, their testimony is not accepted according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is accepted for one thousand. If one testifies to one thousand and the other to one thousand five hundred, and the claimant claims one thousand five hundred, the testimony is accepted for one thousand. If he testifies to one thousand and another says: 'He paid five hundred of it,' his testimony for one thousand is accepted, and his statement is not accepted unless another testifies with him. It is befitting for the witness when he knows that not to testify to one thousand until the claimant admits that he received five hundred. And if two witnesses testify that Zayd was killed on the day of Nahr in Mecca, and two others testify that he was killed on the day of Nahr in Kufa, and they all come together before the judge, he does not accept either testimony. Then marginal notes containing hadith and sayings of the Companions are provided. At the end, Urdu text: 'Principle: If two witnesses are concordant in wording and meaning, their testimony will be accepted according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Principle: The witness testified to one thousand five hundred and the claimant admitted to one thousand; the testimony is not accepted.'
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Testimonies (Kitab al-Shahadat) of al-Quduri presents a series of fundamental rulings governing the acceptance of testimony in Hanafi law. The passage is a ruling statement with proofs (dalil). It opens with the general principle: testimony is accepted only if it agrees with the claim (da'wa). If there is a contradiction, it is rejected. This ensures that testimony directly supports the plaintiff's case. The next ruling addresses the crucial requirement that two witnesses must agree in both wording (lafz) and meaning (ma'na). If they differ in the amount—one says 1000, the other 2000—Abu Hanifa holds that neither is accepted due to the fundamental disagreement. The two disciples (Sahibayn), Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, accept the lower amount (1000) as agreed upon in meaning. The text then applies this: if one says 1000 and the other 1500, and the claimant claims 1500, the testimony is accepted for 1000 only (the lower common amount). A separate case: one witness testifies to a debt of 1000, another states that 500 was paid. The testimony for the 1000 is accepted, but the statement about payment is not accepted unless another witness corroborates it. The author then gives a practical recommendation: a witness who knows of a partial payment should not testify to the full amount until the claimant admits to receiving the payment. Finally, the passage deals with contradictory testimonies on location (Mecca vs. Kufa). If two sets of witnesses give conflicting places for the same event, and they all appear together, the judge does not accept either because reconciliation is impossible. The marginal notes provide hadith proofs (dalil naqli) from the Prophet, sayings of tabi'un like Shuraih and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, and a Quranic verse (2:282) for the general requirement of witnesses. The Urdu summary reiterates the key principles.

Key Terms
الشهادة (al-shahada): Testimony or witness statement in court
الدعوى (al-da'wa): The claim or suit brought by the plaintiff
اتفاق (ittifaq): Agreement between witnesses in wording and meaning

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if one witness testifies to a debt of 1000 dirhams and the other testifies to 2000 dirhams, what happens to their testimony?
A) It is accepted for the lower amount (1000).
B) It is accepted for the higher amount (2000).
C) It is not accepted at all.
D) The judge picks one randomly.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi testimony law, witnesses must agree in wording and meaning; if they differ on amounts, the lower common amount is accepted according to the operative position (Sahibayn).

Precedence of Testimony and Hearsay Exceptions
Rulings on precedence and hearsay exceptions with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rules regarding precedence of testimony and identify the five matters where hearsay testimony is accepted according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Testimony by hearsay is accepted for five specific matters; contradictory later testimony is rejected to ensure judicial finality.

This passage from al-Quduri's Kitab al-Shahadat continues establishing the rules for accepting testimony. It addresses two crucial issues: the effect of precedence when conflicting testimonies appear, and the exceptional cases where a witness may testify without direct observation. Understanding these rules prevents instability in judicial decisions and accommodates the practical realities of proving certain facts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three distinct rulings
Read the passage and list the rulings: (1) if one testimony precedes and judgment is passed, later contradictory testimony is rejected; (2) the judge does not hear jarh (discrediting) or nafi (negation); (3) hearsay is allowed for five specific matters.
These rulings are sequential in the matn.
2
Examine the proof for the precedence rule
The hadith from Ibn al-Musayyib states that if a man gives two contradictory testimonies, the first is accepted and the later is left. This is directly cited in the margin.
Analogously, if two sets of witnesses give contradictory testimonies, the first heard is accepted.
3
Examine the proof for the hearsay exceptions
The hadith of Thuwayba (that she nursed the Prophet and Abu Salama) shows that the Prophet accepted testimony on lineage based on widespread knowledge. The passage cites this as evidence for hearsay on lineage, death, marriage, etc.
The exceptions are based on necessity and istihsan.
4
Apply the hearsay exception to a scenario
Consider a case where a witness testifies to a marriage based on common repute. Under Hanafi law, this is valid because marriage is one of the five exceptions.
The witness does not need to have attended the wedding.
5
Consider the principle of irreconcilable disagreement
The zina example shows that if witnesses disagree on a material detail (location), the hadd punishment is averted. This illustrates that contradictory testimony weakens the case.
This connects to the precedence rule: later contradictory testimony is not heard at all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الشَّهَادَاتِ
٣٦ فان سبقت احدهما وقضى بها ثم حضرت الاخرى لم تقبل الشهادة ٣٧ وَلَا يَسْمَعُ الشَّهَادَةَ عَلَى جُرْح وَلَا نَفْيِ وَلَا يَحْكُمُ بِذَلِكَ الْقَاضِي
وَلا يَجُوزُ لِلشَّاهِدِ أَنْ يَشْهَدَ بِشَيْءٍ لَمْ يُعَايِنُهُ إِلَّا الدَّسَبَ وَالْمَوْتَ وَالنِّكَاحَ وَالدُّخُولَ وَولايَةَ الْقَاضِي فَإِنَّهُ يَسَعُهُ أَنْ يَشْهَدَ بِهَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاءِ إِذَا أَخْبَرَهُ بِمَا مَنْ يَثِقُ بِهِ أَرْبَعَةٍ شَهِدُوا عَلَى امْرَأَةِ بِالزِّنَا، ثُمَّ اخْتَلَفُوا فِي الْمَوْضِعِ، فَقَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ: بِالْكُوفَةِ، وَقَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ: بِالْبَصْرَةِ. قَالَ: «يُدْرَأُ عَنْهُمْ جَمِيعًا » ، » (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ شَهَادَةِ أَرْبَعَةٍ عَلَى امْرَأَةِ بِالزِّنَا وَاخْتِلَافِهُمْ فِي الْمَوْضِع ، نمبر 13380)
٣٦ وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت فان سبقت احدهما وقضى بها \ عَنِ ابْنِ الْمُسَيِّبِ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إِذَا شَهِدَ الرَّجُلُ بِشَهَادَتَيْنِ قُبِلَتِ الْأُولَى، وَتُرِكَتِ الْآخِرَةُ، وَأُنْزِلَ مَنْزِلَةَ الْغُلَامِ»،
أَخْبَرَنَا ، ( » مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ : الرَّجُلُ يَشْهَدُ بِشَهَادَةِ، ثُمَّ يَشْهَدُ بِخِلَافِهَا، نمبر15508) وجه: (۲)قول التابعى لثبوت فان سبقت احدهما وقضى بها أعَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ فِي رَجُلٍ أَشْهَدَ عَلَى شَهَادَتِهِ رَجُلًا، فَقَضَى الْقَاضِي بِشَهَادَتِهِ، ثُمَّ جَاءَ الشَّاهِدُ الَّذِي شَهِدَ عَلَى شَهَادَتِهِ فَقَالَ: لَمْ أَشْهَدْ بِشَيْءٍ قَالَ: يَقُولُ: «إِذَا قَضَى الْقَاضِي مَضَى الْحُكْمُ مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ: الشَّاهِدُ يَرْجِعُ عَنْ شَهَادَتِهِ أَوْ يَشْهَدُ ثُمَّ يَجْحَدُ، نمبر 15512)
۳۷وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت فان سبقت احدهما وقضى بها \ عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِهِ، قَالَ : قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الْمُسْلِمُونَ عُدُولٌ بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَى بَعْضٍ، إِلَّا مَحْدُودًا فِي فِرْيَةٍ»(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه مَنْ قَالَ: لَا تَجُوزُ شَهَادَتُهُ إِذَا تَابَ، غبر 20657)
۳۸ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ لِلشَّاهِدِ أَنْ يَشْهَدَ بِشَيْءٍ لَمْ يُعَايِنْهُ \ وَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَرْضَعَتْنِي وَأَبَا سَلَمَةَ ثُوَيْبَةُ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ الشَّهَادَةِ عَلَى الْأَنْسَابِ وَالرَّضَاعِ الْمُسْتَفِيضِ وَالْمَوْتِ الْقَدِيمِ ،نمبر 2645)
وجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ لِلشَّاهِدِ أَنْ يَشْهَدَ بِشَيْءٍ لَمْ يُعَايِنْهُ وَقَالَ الشَّعْبِيُّ وَابْنُ سِيرِينَ وَعَطَاءٌ وَقَتَادَةُ السَّمْعُ شَهَادَةً وَكَانَ الْحَسَنُ يَقُولُ لَمْ يُشْهِدُونِي عَلَى شَيْءٍ وَإِنِّي سَمِعْتُ كَذَا اصول: فیصلہ سے پہلے دونوں گواہوں میں ایسا اختلاف ہو جائے کہ موافقت نا ممکن ہو تو دونوں کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائیں گی۔
The Book of Testimonies. 36: If one of them preceded and judgment was passed based on it, then the other comes, the testimony is not accepted. 37: The judge does not hear testimony regarding discrediting (jarh) nor negation (nafi), nor does he rule based on that. It is not permissible for a witness to testify to something he did not witness except lineage, death, marriage, entering, and the appointment of a judge; for it is permissible for him to testify to these things if informed by someone he trusts. Four witnesses testified against a woman for zina, then they differed on the location: some said Kufa, some said Basra. He said: 'The punishment is averted from all of them.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) Then marginal notes with hadith and athar. Finally, Urdu: 'Principle: If before judgment such a disagreement occurs between two witnesses that reconciliation is impossible, then both testimonies are not accepted.'
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri continues with more rulings on testimony. First, if one set of witnesses presents their testimony and judgment is based on it, and then another set comes with contradictory testimony, the later testimony is not accepted. This prevents instability in judgments. The next ruling states that the judge does not hear testimony regarding jarh (discrediting a witness) or nafi (negation of something), and does not rule based on it; this means that a person cannot simply claim that a witness is disqualified without proper evidence. The third ruling is an important exception to the general rule that a witness must have direct observation (mu'ayana). Testimony by hearsay (shahada bil-istifada) is allowed for five specific matters: lineage (nasab), death (mawt), marriage (nikah), entering (dukhul, i.e., consummation), and the appointment of a judge (wilayat al-qadi). These matters are difficult to prove by direct observation because they are ongoing or well-known. The witness may testify based on widespread knowledge or reliable information from a trustworthy source. The passage then gives an example: if four witnesses testify to zina but differ on the location, the hadd punishment is averted from them all. This shows that disagreement in testimony can lead to rejection. The marginal notes provide hadith proofs: a hadith from Ibn al-Musayyib that if a man testifies with two testimonies (contradictory), the first is accepted and the later is left; a hadith from Amr ibn Shu'ayb that Muslims are upright unless punished for false accusation; and the hadith about Thuwayba's being a wet nurse to the Prophet, used as evidence for hearsay on lineage. The Urdu summary reiterates the principle of irreconcilable disagreement leading to rejection.

Key Terms
الجَرْح (al-jarh): Discrediting or impeaching a witness's character
النَّفى (al-nafi): Negation; claiming that something (like a right) does not exist
الاستفاضة (al-istifada): Widespread repute or hearsay accepted as evidence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, for which of the following can a witness testify based on hearsay (shahada bil-istifada)?
A) A debt of 1000 dirhams
B) A marriage contract
C) A theft
D) A contract of sale

Key Takeaway
Hanafi law allows hearsay testimony for five specific matters (lineage, death, marriage, entry, appointment of judge) and rejects later contradictory testimony after judgment, ensuring finality and practicality.

Shahadat — Testimony

Testimony Upon Testimony: Scope and Conditions
States the permissibility and scope of testimony upon testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for accepting testimony upon testimony in the Hanafi school and identify the cases where it is rejected.

Core Idea
Testimony upon testimony is accepted for rights but not hudud/qisas — certainty demands.

In Islamic courts, direct witness testimony is typically required. However, necessity sometimes calls for indirect testimony—a witness testifying on behalf of another witness. This passage from Al-Quduri lays down the Hanafi position: such testimony is generally permissible for financial and property rights, but not for serious criminal penalties where certainty is paramount. Understanding this distinction is crucial for comprehending how Islamic evidence law balances truth and caution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'shahada 'ala al-shahada' (testimony upon testimony). The ruling is 'ja'iz' (permissible/accepted).
Ja'iz here means legally valid and admissible in court.
2
Determine the scope of permissibility
It is accepted 'fi kulli haqqin la yasqutu bil-shubha'—in every right that is not nullified by doubt. This covers financial rights and property claims.
Examples: debt, sale, lease, inheritance.
3
Identify the exceptions
It is NOT accepted in hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation). These require the highest certainty.
Hudud include theft, fornication, drinking. Qisas covers murder and bodily harm.
4
Specify the witness requirement
Two branch witnesses must testify on behalf of two original witnesses. One branch witness testifying for one original witness is not accepted.
This preserves the evidentiary standard of two witnesses for claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالشَّهَادَةُ عَلَى الشَّهَادَةِ جَائِزَةٌ فِي كُلِّ حَقٍّ لَا يَسْقُطُ بِالشُّبْهَةِ وَلَا تُقْبَلُ فِي الْحُدُودِ وَالْقِصَاصِ وَيَجُوزُ شَهَادَةُ شَاهِدَيْنِ عَلَى شَهَادَةِ شَاهِدَيْنِ وَلَا تُقْبَلُ شَهَادَةُ وَاحِدٍ عَلَى شَهَادَةِ وَاحِدٍ
Testimony upon testimony is permissible in every right that is not nullified by doubt, and it is not accepted in [cases of] prescribed punishments (hudud) and retribution (qisas). And the testimony of two witnesses upon the testimony of two witnesses is permissible, and the testimony of one upon the testimony of one is not accepted.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage states a foundational ruling from Kitab al-Shahadat (Book of Testimonies) in the Hanafi madhhab regarding indirect testimony. The principle is that 'shahada 'ala al-shahada' (testimony based on another witness's statement) is valid in all matters of financial rights and property claims, because these rights are not automatically dropped by the presence of doubt (shubha). However, such indirect testimony is not accepted in cases of hudud (fixed punishments for crimes like theft or adultery) and qisas (retaliation for murder or bodily harm) because these penalties require the highest level of certainty. Furthermore, the rule requires that two branch witnesses (shuhud al-far') testify on behalf of two original witnesses (shuhud al-asl); a single witness cannot testify on behalf of another single witness, as the original burden of proof cannot be reduced.

Key Terms
الشَّهَادَةُ عَلَى الشَّهَادَةِ (al-shahada 'ala al-shahada): Testimony given by a branch witness (shahid al-far') based on the testimony of the original witness (shahid al-asl).
الْحُدُودُ (al-hudud): Fixed corporal punishments prescribed by the Qur'an and Sunnah for specific major sins, such as theft, fornication, drinking alcohol, etc.
الْقِصَاصُ (al-qisas): Retributive justice: the right of the victim or his heirs to demand retaliation for murder or bodily harm.
لَا يَسْقُطُ بِالشُّبْهَةِ (la yasqutu bil-shubha): Not nullified by doubt; refers to rights that remain valid even when there is some uncertainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada) is NOT accepted in which of the following?
A) Financial rights like debts and loans
B) Cases of hudud and qisas
C) Marriage contracts
D) Wills and bequests

Key Takeaway
Testimony upon testimony is a valid form of evidence in Hanafi law for financial and property rights, but not for hudud and qisas; it always requires two branch witnesses to replace two original witnesses.

Procedure and Conditions for Testimony Upon Testimony
Procedure and conditions for branch testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prescribed wording for deputizing a branch witness and identify the three conditions that make branch testimony admissible in Hanafi law.

Core Idea
Branch testimony is only accepted when the original witness explicitly deputizes the branch and direct testimony is impossible.

This lesson focuses on the specific Hanafi procedure for testimony upon testimony (shahada ala al-shahada). You will learn the exact wording that must be used by both the original and branch witnesses, and the circumstances under which branch testimony becomes acceptable. This is a practical ruling that ensures the chain of testimony is clear and reliable when the original witness cannot appear in court.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Recognize the two roles: shahid al-asl (original witness) who directly witnessed the event, and shahid al-far' (branch witness) who testifies based on the original's testimony.
The original is the primary source; the branch is a substitute under necessity.
2
Understand the deputization formula
The original must explicitly deputize the branch by saying: 'Testify on my testimony, i.e., I testify that so-and-so acknowledged before me such-and-such, and he took me as a witness against himself.'
The phrase 'he took me as a witness against himself' is not essential; if omitted, the deputization is still valid.
3
Learn the branch's testimony formula
When testifying in court, the branch must use a specific formula: 'I testify that so-and-so (the original) made me testify on his testimony that he testifies that so-and-so acknowledged such-and-such, and he said to me: testify on my testimony to that.'
This ensures the chain from original to branch is clearly stated.
4
Know the conditions for acceptance
Branch testimony is only accepted if: 1) The original witnesses have died, 2) They are absent at a distance of three days' travel or more, or 3) They are sick with an illness that prevents them from attending court.
These conditions reflect the principle of necessity (darura).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَصِفَةُ الْإِشْهَادِ أَنْ يَقُولَ شَاهِدُ الْأَصْلِ لِشَاهِدِ الْفَرْعِ: اشْهَدْ عَلَى شَهَادَتِي أَيْ أَشْهَدُ أَنَّ فُلَانَ بْنَ فُلَانٍ أَقَرَّ عِنْدِي بِكَذَا وَأَشْهَدَنِي عَلَى نَفْسِهِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَقُلْ أَشْهَدَنِي عَلَى نَفْسِهِ جَازَ وَيَقُولُ شَاهِدُ الْفَرْعِ عِنْدَ الْأَدَاءِ: أَشْهَدُ أَنَّ فُلَانًا أَشْهَدَنِي عَلَى شَهَادَتِهِ أَنَّهُ يَشْهَدُ أَنَّ فُلَانًا أَقَرَّ عِنْدَهُ بِكَذَا وَقَالَ لِي: اشْهَدْ عَلَى شَهَادَتِي بِذَلِكَ وَلَا تُقْبَلُ شَهَادَةُ شُهُودِ الْفَرْعِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَمُوتَ شُهُودُ الْأَصْلِ أَوْ يَغِيبُوا مَسِيرَةَ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فَصَاعِدًا أَوْ يَمْرَضُوا مَرَضًا لَا يَسْتَطِيعُونَ مَعَهُ حُضُورَ مَجْلِسِ الْحَاكِمِ
And the description of taking testimony is that the original witness says to the branch witness: 'Testify on my testimony, i.e., I testify that so-and-so acknowledged before me such-and-such, and he took me as a witness against himself.' And if he does not say 'he took me as a witness against himself,' it is permissible. And the branch witness says when testifying: 'I testify that so-and-so made me testify on his testimony that he testifies that so-and-so acknowledged before him such-and-such, and he said to me: testify on my testimony to that.' And the testimony of branch witnesses is not accepted unless the original witnesses have died, or they are absent at a distance of three days' travel or more, or they are sick with an illness that prevents them from attending the court of the judge.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage details the proper procedure (sifat al-ishhad) for establishing testimony upon testimony. The original witness (shahid al-asl) must explicitly deputize the branch witness (shahid al-far') by saying 'Testify on my testimony' and then stating the content, e.g., 'I testify that Zayd acknowledged debt of X' and 'he took me as a witness against himself.' However, the latter phrase is not strictly necessary; if omitted, the deputation remains valid. The branch witness, when recounting the testimony in court, must use a specific formula: 'I testify that so-and-so (the original witness) made me testify on his testimony that he testifies that so-and-so acknowledged such-and-such, and he said to me: testify on my testimony to that.' This ensures the chain is clear. Additionally, branch testimony is only accepted when direct testimony from the original witness is impossible due to their death, long-term absence (3 days' travel distance or more), or incapacitating illness. This reflects the principle that the original witness is the primary source, and the branch is only a substitute under necessity.

Key Terms
شَاهِدُ الْأَصْلِ (shahid al-asl): The original witness who directly witnessed the event or heard the acknowledgment.
شَاهِدُ الْفَرْعِ (shahid al-far'): The branch witness who testifies based on the testimony of the original witness.
الْإِشْهَادُ (al-ishhad): The act of formally requesting someone to witness one's own testimony, i.e., deputization.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What two conditions allow branch testimony to be accepted?
A) The original witnesses are absent for any reason and the branch witnesses are reliable
B) The original witnesses are dead, absent for at least three days' travel, or too sick to attend court
C) The original witnesses give written permission
D) The case involves hudud or qisas

Key Takeaway
Branch testimony is only accepted when direct testimony is impossible and the original witness explicitly deputizes the branch using prescribed wording.

Punishment of False Witness: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Presents intra-Hanafi dispute on ta'zir for false witness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on punishment for false witness and distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa punishes false witness by public shaming only; the Sahibayn add beating and imprisonment.

This short passage captures an important intra-Hanafi dispute about how to punish a false witness. While all agree that the act is a major sin, the mode of punishment differs. Understanding this ikhtilaf helps you see how the Hanafi school deliberates evidence (athar vs qiyas) and how the mufta bihi is determined.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognize that false witness (shāhid al-zūr) is a sin without a fixed hadd; its punishment is ta'zir (discretionary).
Ta'zir can include shaming, beating, imprisonment, etc., but must not exceed the lowest hadd (40 lashes).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa orders tashhīr (public shaming in the market) and explicitly refuses any further ta'zir (beating or imprisonment).
His proof: the precedent of Umar ibn al-Khattab who shamed a false witness.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani differ: they prescribe painful beating and imprisonment.
Their proof: qiyas on other crimes of falsehood that require corporal deterrence.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa's view, the witness is only shamed and released; under the Sahibayn, he suffers beatings and detention. This affects the severity of punishment in practice.
Though the text does not give tarjih, the Hanafi school relies on Abu Hanifa's view in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ فِي شَاهِدِ الزُّورِ: أَشْهَرُهُ فِي السُّوقِ وَلَا أُعَزِّرُهُ. وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ: نُوجِعُهُ ضَرْبًا وَنَحْبِسُهُ.
And Abu Hanifa said concerning the false witness: 'I will publicize him in the market and I will not impose ta'zir on him.' And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: 'We inflict painful beating upon him and imprison him.'
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the punishment for a false witness. The passage states the position of Abu Hanifa: he prescribes tashhir (public shaming) by announcing the person's falsehood in the market, but does not impose any additional ta'zir (discretionary punishment). His reasoning is that the infamy of public shaming is sufficient deterrence. In contrast, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the false witness should be subjected to corporal punishment (beating) and imprisonment. In the Hanafi madhhab, Abu Hanifa's view is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) as recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah, though later practice has varied.

Key Terms
شَاهِدُ الزُّورِ (shāhid al-zūr): A false witness; one who knowingly gives false testimony in court.
تَشْهِير (tashhīr): Public shaming by announcing the person's offense in the marketplace.
تَعْزِير (taʿzīr): Discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd (Quranic punishment).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is Abu Hanifa's position on punishment for a false witness?
A) Flogging and imprisonment.
B) Public shaming only, no ta'zir beating.
C) Amputation of hand.
D) No punishment at all.

Key Takeaway
A false witness receives ta'zir; Abu Hanifa holds that public shaming (tashhir) suffices, while the Sahibayn add beating and imprisonment.

Original Witnesses Certifying Substitute Witnesses
Ruling on the effect of original witnesses' attestation on substitute testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when original witnesses certify, remain silent, or deny the testimony of substitute witnesses, and identify the proof from Shurayh's practice.

Core Idea
Substitute testimony is accepted unless the original witnesses deny it — silence with judge investigation suffices.

This passage from Al-Quduri's Kitab al-Shahadat presents three scenarios regarding the effect of original witnesses' stance on substitute testimony. It also provides the evidential basis from the practice of the early judge Shurayh. Understanding this ruling is essential for correctly applying the rules of testimony in Islamic courts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
List the three possible reactions of the original witnesses (shuhud al-asl) regarding the substitutes (shuhud al-far'): explicit certification, silence, or outright denial of having testified.
These scenarios cover all possibilities.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
If they certify the substitutes, substitute testimony is accepted. If they remain silent, it is also accepted but the judge must investigate their condition. If they deny their own testimony, the substitute testimony is rejected.
The ruling differentiates between silence and denial.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is from Shurayh's instruction: 'Say: I testify on the authority of a just person' (قُلْ أَشْهَدَي ذُو عَدْلٍ) and his general acceptance of testimony upon testimony.
Both are recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Shurayh's statement indicates that the substitute witness must explicitly attribute the testimony to a just person (the original witness). This implies that certification by the original is sufficient, and silence does not break the chain.
The practice shows that the judge (Shurayh) accepted the substitute testimony when the witness declared the original was just.
5
Note the role of the judge
When the original witnesses are silent, the judge must independently examine the condition of the original witnesses to ensure their justice.
This prevents abuse while allowing the process to proceed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الشَّهَادَاتِ فَإِنْ عَدَّلَ شُهُودُ الْأَصْلِ شُهُودَ الْفَرْعِ جَازَ وَإِنْ سَكَتُوا عَنْ تَعْدِيلِهِمْ جَازَ وَيَنْظُرُ الْحَاكِمُ فِي حَالِهِمْ وَإِنْ أَنْكَرَ شُهُودُ الْأَصْلِ الشَّهَادَةَ لَمْ تُقْبَلْ شَهَادَةُ الْفُرُوعِ 
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ عَدَّلَ شُهُودُ الْأَصْل شُهُودَ الْفَرْعِ جَازَا وَيَقُولُ شُرَيْحٌ لِلشَّاهِدِ: "قُلْ أَشْهَدَي ذُو عَدْلٍ" (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ : شَهَادَةُ الرَّجُلِ عَلَى الرَّجُلِ، 15447) 
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ أَنْكَرَ شُهُودُ الْأَصْلِ الشَّهَادَةَ لَمْ تُقْبَلْ شَهَادَةُ الْفُرُوعِ 
عَنْ حَسَنِ بْنِ صَالِحٍ، قَالَ: قُلْتُ لِلْجَعْدِ بْنِ ذَكْوَانَ : شَهِدْتَ شُرَيْئًا يَقُولُ: «أُجِيزُ شَهَادَةَ الشَّاهِدِ عَلَى الشَّاهِدِ إِذَا شَهِدَ عَلَيْهِمَا » ، » (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي شَهَادَةِ الشَّاهِدِ عَلَى الشَّاهِدِ، نمبر 23078) 
اصول: فرع پر اصل کے عادل ہونے کو جاننا بھی ضروری ہے تا کہ گواہی میں اطمینان ہو۔ اصول: نسب بیان کر کے گواہی دی لیکن فرع گواہ چہرہ سے نا آشنا ہو تو دوسری گواہی دینی ہوگی۔
Book of Testimonies: If the original witnesses certify the substitute witnesses, it is permissible; and if they remain silent about their certification, it is permissible, and the judge looks into their condition. And if the original witnesses deny the testimony, the testimony of the substitutes is not accepted. Proof: (1) Statement of a tabi'i for confirmation: If the original witnesses certify the substitute witnesses, it is permissible, and Shurayh used to say to the witness: 'Say: I testify on the authority of a just person'. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Book: Testimony of a man on a man, 15447). Proof: (1) Statement of a tabi'i for confirmation: And if the original witnesses deny the testimony, the testimony of the substitutes is not accepted. From Hasan ibn Salih, he said: I said to al-Ja'd ibn Dhakwan: Did you witness Shurayh saying: 'I accept the testimony of the witness upon the witness when he testifies against them'? (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, On the testimony of the witness upon the witness, no. 23078). Principle: It is also necessary to know the original witnesses to be just concerning the substitute so that there is confidence in the testimony. Principle: If the original witnesses gave testimony by stating lineage but the substitute witness is unfamiliar with the face, then another testimony must be given.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's Kitab al-Shahadat presents the ruling on the validity of substitute testimony (shahadat al-far') when the original witnesses (shuhud al-asl) have different reactions. The ruling states that if the original witnesses explicitly certify the substitutes as just, then the substitute testimony is accepted. If they remain silent about certification, it is also accepted, but the judge must examine their condition (i.e., their reliability). However, if the original witnesses deny having given testimony altogether, then the substitute testimony is not accepted. The accompanying proofs include the practice of Shurayh, a famous judge, who instructed the witness to state 'I testify on the authority of a just person,' indicating that certification is valid. Another proof from Shurayh shows that he accepted testimony upon testimony when the witness testifies against the original witnesses. The Urdu commentary adds that knowing the original witnesses to be just is necessary for confidence, and if the substitute does not recognize the face due to lineage-based testimony, another testimony is needed.

Key Terms
شُهُودُ الْأَصْلِ (shuhud al-asl): The original witnesses who directly witnessed the event and whose testimony is being used as a basis for substitute witnesses.
شُهُودُ الْفَرْعِ (shuhud al-far'): Substitute witnesses who testify on the basis of the original witnesses' testimony.
تَعْدِيل (ta'dil): Certification of a witness's justice and reliability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If original witnesses remain silent about certifying the substitute witnesses, what is the ruling?
A) The substitute testimony is rejected.
B) The substitute testimony is accepted and the judge need not investigate.
C) The substitute testimony is accepted, but the judge must investigate their condition.
D) The substitute testimony is accepted only if the original witnesses explicitly deny it.

Key Takeaway
Substitute testimony is valid when original witnesses certify or remain silent (with judge investigation), but invalid if the original witnesses deny the testimony.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Punishment of False Witness
Abu Hanifa's view vs Sahibayn on ta'zir for false witness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the punishment of a false witness and identify the evidence used by each side.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa punishes false witness with public shaming; the Sahibayn add beating and imprisonment.

This passage presents a disagreement among the Hanafi imams regarding the appropriate punishment for a false witness (shahid al-zur). While they agree that ta'zir is the category of punishment, they differ on whether it should be physical or merely reputational. Understanding this dispute reveals the role of Companion practice as a source of law and the limits of discretionary punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Locate the statement of Abu Hanifa and the statement of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn). Note the difference in punishment: tashhir (publicizing) vs. beating and imprisonment.
Abu Hanifa says: 'I publicize him and do not give ta'zir.' The Sahibayn say: 'We beat him severely and imprison him.'
2
Examine the proof for the Sahibayn's position
The text provides two proofs: the Quranic verse 'Avoid false speech' (Quran 22:30) and the practice of Caliph Umar who flogged, blackened the face, shaved the head, and imprisoned a false witness. Understand that these proofs support the Sahibayn's view.
Umar's practice is recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
3
Note the principle of ta'zir
The Urdu commentary defines ta'zir as discretionary punishment, with a maximum of less than forty lashes. This frame helps understand why Abu Hanifa can choose tashhir over beating.
Ta'zir is not a fixed hadd; the judge has discretion within bounds.
4
Determine the practical difference
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifa, the false witness avoids physical pain but suffers public disgrace; under the Sahibayn, he is corporally punished and imprisoned.
This affects the deterrent effect and the severity of the punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ فِي شَاهِدِ الزور: أَشْهرُهُ في السُّوقِ وَلا أُعَزَرُهُ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ: نُوجِعُهُ ضَرْبًا وَتَحْبِسُهُ 
وجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت فَاجْتَنِبُوا الرِّجْسَ مِنَ الْأَوْثَنِ وَاجْتَنِبُوا قَوْلَ النُّورِ ﴾ (سورة الحج، 22 آيت نمبر 30) وجه:(۲)قول الصحابي لثبوت أَنَّ عُمَرَ بْنَ الْخَطَّابِ كَتَبَ إِلَى عُمَّالِهِ بِالشَّامِ فِي شَاهِدِ النُّورِ أَنْ يُجْلَدَ أَرْبَعِينَ جَلْدَةً، وَأَنْ يُسْخَمَ وَجْهُهُ وَأَنْ يُخْلَقَ رَأْسُهُ وَأَنْ يُطَالَ حَبْسُهُ (مصنف عبد الرزاق ، بَ : عُقُوبَةُ شَاهِدِ النُّورِ، ن15392) ٢٨ وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت عَنْ مَكْحُولِ، «أَنَّ عُمَرَ بْنَ الْخَطَّابِ ضَرَبَ شَاهِدَ زُورٍ أَرْبَعِينَ سَوْطًا » ، مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ: عُقُوبَةُ شَاهِدِ الزور، نمبر 15396 مصنف ابن ابي شيبه شَاهِدُ النُّورِ مَا يُصْنَعُ بِهِ، نمبر 23047) 
اصول: تعزیر اس جرم کی سزا کو کہتے ہیں جو تنبیہ اور تذلیل کے لئے ہو جس کی شریعت میں حد متعین نہ ہو البتہ تعزیر میں سزا چالیس کوڑے سے کم ہو گی۔ لغات: الزور : جھوٹا، أَشَهرُ : تشہیر کرتا، أَعَزَرُ : سزا دینا، نُوجعُهُ : ضَرْبًا : مارتا، تحبس : قید کرنا، سخم: منھ کالا کرنا
And Abu Hanifa said concerning the false witness: I publicize him in the market and I do not give him ta'zir. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: We beat him severely and imprison him. Proof: (1) The verse for confirmation: 'So avoid the abomination of idols and avoid false speech' (Surah al-Hajj, 22:30). Proof: (2) Statement of a companion for confirmation: That Umar ibn al-Khattab wrote to his governors in Syria concerning the false witness: that he should be flogged forty lashes, his face should be blackened, his head should be shaved, and his imprisonment should be prolonged. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Book: Punishment of the false witness, no. 15392). Proof: (1) Statement of a tabi'i for confirmation: From Makhul that Umar ibn al-Khattab beat a false witness forty lashes. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Book: Punishment of false witness, no. 15396; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, What is done with the false witness, no. 23047). Principle: Ta'zir is the punishment for a crime that is for admonition and humiliation, for which the Shari'ah has not specified a fixed penalty; however, in ta'zir the punishment is less than forty lashes. Vocabulary: al-zur: false; ashharu: publicize; u'azziru: give ta'zir; nuji'uhu: beat; darban: beating; tahbis: imprison; sakhkham: blacken the face.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the punishment of a false witness (shahid al-zur). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the witness should be publicly disgraced (tashhir) in the market but should not receive physical ta'zir (discretionary beating). In contrast, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the witness should be severely beaten and imprisoned. The proofs provided include the Quranic verse commanding avoidance of false speech (qawl al-zur) as a basis for punishment, and actions of Caliph Umar who ordered forty lashes, blackening the face, shaving the head, and prolonged imprisonment for a false witness. Another narration from Makhul confirms that Umar beat a false witness forty lashes. The Urdu commentary explains that ta'zir is a discretionary punishment with a maximum of forty lashes, and provides vocabulary for key terms.

Key Terms
شَاهِدُ الزُّورِ (shahid al-zur): A witness who gives false testimony intentionally.
تَعْزِير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for crimes without fixed hadd, intended for admonition; maximum less than forty lashes.
تَشْهِير (tashhir): Publicizing a person's crime to disgrace them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the punishment for a false witness?
A) Flogging forty lashes
B) Imprisonment only
C) Publicizing in the market and no ta'zir
D) Beating and blackening the face

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the punishment for false witness is discretionary (ta'zir), with Abu Hanifa favoring public shaming and the Sahibayn adding corporal punishment.

Witness Retraction Before and After Judgment
Ruling on witness retraction before and after judicial verdict with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on witness retraction before and after judgment, and apply the rule of daman (liability) accordingly.

Core Idea
Retract before judgment: no liability; retract after judgment: verdict stands, but you pay.

This lesson from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar examines a key procedural ruling in Islamic judicial proceedings: what happens when witnesses withdraw their testimony? The ruling distinguishes between retraction before and after the judge's verdict, balancing finality of judgments with accountability for harm caused. The Hanafi school, relying on hadith and the practice of Caliph 'Ali, provides a clear framework that you will now analyze.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text explicitly distinguishes between retraction before judgment and retraction after judgment. Note the different consequences for each.
2
Locate the ruling for each scenario
Before judgment: testimony is dropped (saqata) and no liability (daman). After judgment: the verdict is not overturned (la yufsakh) and witnesses are liable for damages.
3
Examine the proofs (dalil)
For before judgment: hadith of Ma'iz (SAW disapproved persistence) and statement of al-Zuhri. For after judgment: action of 'Ali (paid diyah, kept verdict) and statement of al-Nuri.
Both proofs are zanni in transmission and indication.
4
Understand the legal principle (asl)
The Urdu commentary adds: 'He who causes damage is liable for that damage.' This underlies the after-judgment liability.
5
Apply the ruling to a hypothetical
Consider a case where witnesses testify to theft, judge cuts off hand, then witnesses retract. Apply the rule: verdict stands, witnesses pay diyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - ! إِذَا رَجَعَ الشُّهُودُ عَنْ شَهَادَتِهِمْ قَبْلَ الْحُكْمِ بِمَا سَقَطَتْ وَلَا ضَمَانَ عَلَيْهِمْ فَإِنْ حُكِمَ بِشَهَادَتِيمْ ثُمَّ رَجَعُوا لَمْ يُفْسَخُ الْحُكْمُ وَوَجَبَ عَلَيْهِمْ ضَمَانُ مَا أَتْلَفُوهُ بِشَهَادَقِهِمْ 
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت إذَا رَجَعَ الشُّهُودُ عَنْ شَهَادَتِهِمْ قَبْلَ الْحُكْمِ 
حَدَّثَنِي يَزِيدُ بْنُ نُعَيْمِ بْنِ هَزَّالٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، قَالَ: كَانَ مَاعِزُ بْنُ مَالِكِ يَتِيمًا ثُمَّ أَتَى النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَذَكَرَ ذَلِكَ لَهُ، فَقَالَ: «هَلَّا تَرَكْتُمُوهُ لَعَلَّهُ أَنْ يَتُوبَ، فَيَتُوبَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ» (سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابُ رَجْمِ مَاعِزِ بْنِ مَالِك، نمبر 4419) 
وجه : (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت إذَا رَجَعَ الشُّهُودُ عَنْ شَهَادَتِهِمْ قَبْلَ الحُكْمِ 
سَأَلْتُ الزُّهْرِيَّ عَنْ رَجُلٍ شَهِدَ عِنْدَ الْإِمَامِ، فَأَثْبَتَ الْإِمَامُ شَهَادَتَهُ، ثُمَّ دُعِيَ لَهَا فَبَدَّهَا، أَتَجُوزُ شَهَادَتْهُ الْأُولَى، أَوِ الْآخِرَةُ؟ قَالَ: " لا شَهَادَةَ لَهُ فِي الأُولَى وَلا فِي الْآخِرَةِ ". قَالَ الشَّيْخُ: " وَهَذَا فِي الرُّجُوعِ قَبْلَ إِمْضَاءِ الْحُكْمِ بِالْأُولَى "،(السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ : الرُّجُوعُ عَنِ الشَّهَادَةِ، نمبر 21195) 
لوجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ حَكِمَ بِشَهَادَتِهِمْ ثُمَّ رَجَعُوا لَمْ يُفْسَخُ الْحَكْمُ 
عَنِ الشَّعْبِي، أَنَّ رَجُلَيْنِ شَهِدَا عِنْدَ عَلِي هِ عَلَى رَجُلٍ بِالسَّرِقَةِ، فَقَطَعَ عَلِيٌّ يَدَهُ، ثُمَّ جَاءَا بِآخَرَ فَقَالَا: هَذَا هُوَ السَّارِقُ، لَا الْأَوَّلُ، فَأَغَرَمَ عَلِيٌّ له الشَّاهِدَيْنِ دِيَةَ يَدِ الْمَقْطُوعِ الْأَوَّلِ، وَقَالَ: " لَوْ أَعْلَمُ أَنَّكُمَا تَعَمَّدْتُمَا لَقَطَعْتُ أَيْدِيَكُمَا " ، وَلَمْ يَقْطَع الثَّانِي، ( السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ : الرُّجُوعُ عَنِ الشَّهَادَةِ، نمبر 21192/مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ: الشَّاهِدُ يَرْجِعُ عَنْ شَهَادَتِهِ أَوْ يَشْهَدُ ثُمَّ يَجْحَدُ ، نمبر 15512) 
وجه : (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ حُكِمَ بِشَهَادَتِهِمْ ثُمَّ رَجَعُوا لَمْ يُفْسَخُ الْحُكْمُ 
عَنِ النَّوْرِي فِي رَجُلٍ أَشْهَدَ عَلَى شَهَادَتِهِ رَجُلًا، فَقَضَى الْقَاضِي بِشَهَادَتِهِ، ثُمَّ جَاءَ الشَّاهِدُ الَّذِي شَهِدَ عَلَى شَهَادَتِهِ فَقَالَ: لَمْ أَشْهَدْ بِشَيْءٍ قَالَ: يَقُولُ: «إِذَا قَضَى الْقَاضِي مَضَى الحَكْمُ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق بَابٌ : الشَّاهِدُ يَرْجِعُ عَنْ شَهَادَتِهِ أَوْ يَشْهَدُ ثُمَّ يَجْحَدُ ، نمبر 15512/»،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه الشَّاهِدَانِ يَشْهَدَانِ ثُمَّ يَرْجِعُ أَحَدُهُمَا ، غمبر 22558) 
اصول: جس نے جس کا جتنا نقصان کیا وہ اتنے کا ذمہ دار ہو گا۔
اصول: فیصلہ سے قبل اگر رجوع کر جائے تو دوسری یا تیسری کسی گواہی کا اعتبار نہیں، اور نہ ضمان ہو گا۔
He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him -: When the witnesses retract their testimony before judgment, it is dropped and there is no liability on them. If judgment is passed on their testimony and then they retract, the judgment is not overturned, and they are liable for the damage they caused by their testimony. Proof: (1) Hadith for confirmation: When witnesses retract before judgment: Yazid ibn Nu'aym ibn Hazzal narrated from his father: Ma'iz ibn Malik was an orphan; then he came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and mentioned that... So he said: 'Why did you not leave him; perhaps he would repent, and Allah would accept his repentance.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Book: Stoning of Ma'iz ibn Malik, no. 4419). Proof: (2) Statement of a tabi'i for confirmation: When witnesses retract before judgment: I asked al-Zuhri about a man who testified before the imam, and the imam established his testimony, then he was called for it and he changed it. He said: 'There is no testimony for him in the first nor in the second.' The shaykh said: 'This is about retraction before the execution of the first judgment.' (Sunan al-Kubra li al-Bayhaqi, Book: Retraction of testimony, no. 21195). Proof: (1) Statement of a tabi'i for confirmation: If judgment is passed on their testimony and then they retract, the judgment is not overturned: From al-Sha'bi that two men testified before 'Ali against a man for theft, so 'Ali cut off his hand. Then they brought another and said: 'This is the thief, not the first.' So 'Ali made the two witnesses pay the blood money for the first man's cut hand, and said: 'If I knew that you did it deliberately, I would cut off your hands.' And he did not cut off the second. (Sunan al-Kubra li al-Bayhaqi, ...). Proof: (2) Statement of a tabi'i for confirmation: If judgment is passed on their testimony and then they retract, the judgment is not overturned: From al-Nuri (?) concerning a man who had another witness upon his testimony, and the judge decided on his testimony, then the witness who testified upon his testimony came and said: 'I did not testify to anything.' He said: 'When the judge decides, the judgment stands.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, ...). Principle: He who causes damage is liable for that damage. Principle: If retraction occurs before the decision, then no second or third testimony is accepted, and there is no liability.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Retraction of Testimony provides the ruling on the legal effect of witnesses retracting their testimony at different stages. If they retract before the judge issues his verdict, their testimony is considered void (saqata) and they bear no financial liability (daman). However, if the verdict has already been issued based on their testimony and they subsequently retract, the verdict remains in force (la yufsakh) and they become liable for the damages caused by their testimony. The proofs include the hadith of Ma'iz where the Prophet disapproved of the witnesses' persistence, implying that retraction before judgment would have nullified the testimony. The example of Caliph 'Ali shows that after judgment (amputation), when witnesses retracted, he did not overturn the judgment but made them pay diyah. The Urdu commentary summarizes: liability is according to the damage; retraction before verdict nullifies testimony with no liability.

Key Terms
رَجَعَ عَنْ الشَّهَادَةِ (raja'a 'an al-shahada): To withdraw or take back one's testimony.
ضَمَان (daman): Financial liability or compensation for damages caused.
نَقْضُ الْحُكْم (naqd al-hukm): Overturning a judicial verdict.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if witnesses retract their testimony after the judge has issued a verdict based on it?
A) The verdict is overturned and witnesses are not liable.
B) The verdict stands and witnesses are liable for damages.
C) The verdict is overturned and witnesses are liable.
D) The verdict stands and witnesses are not liable.

Key Takeaway
Retraction before judgment nullifies testimony with no liability; retraction after judgment leaves the verdict intact but imposes liability for damages.

Rulings on Retraction of Testimony
Hanafi rulings and evidence on witness retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retraction of testimony before and after judgment, and apply the apportionment rules when one or more witnesses retract.

Core Idea
Testimony retraction before judgment voids it; after judgment, the verdict stands but witnesses compensate.

This lesson examines the legal consequences when witnesses withdraw their testimony (al-ruju' 'an al-shahadah) in Hanafi fiqh. The timing of retraction—before or after the judge's ruling—dramatically changes the outcome: before judgment the testimony is simply dropped; after judgment the verdict remains binding, but the witnesses become liable for the loss they caused. We also explore how liability is shared when multiple witnesses testify and some retract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon (retraction of testimony) and identify the two distinct timeframes: before judgment and after judgment. For each, note the hukm (legal effect).
2
Locate the dalil
The passage itself does not explicitly quote the dalil, but the Hanafi proof is drawn from the Quranic principle of equivalent compensation (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:45) applied by analogy (qiyas) to financial loss caused by false testimony.
The dalil is not in the matn but is part of the sharh tradition.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does Quran 5:45 support the ruling? The verse establishes qisas for bodily harm, which is extended to financial harm via qiyas jali. Since the witnesses caused the loss, they must compensate.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that retraction after judgment invalidates the verdict. The Hanafi position is that the judgment stands, and only compensation is due.
The text does not elaborate, but this is a well-known difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الرُّجُوعِ عَنْ الشَّهَادَةِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - : إِذَا رَجَعَ الشُّهُودُ عَنْ شَهَادَتِهِمْ قَبْلَ الْحُكْمِ بِمَا سَقَطَتْ وَلَا ضَمَانَ عَلَيْهِمْ
فَإِنْ حُكِمَ بِشَهَادَتِهِمْ ثُمَّ رَجَعُوا لَمْ يُفْسَخُ الْحُكْمُ وَوَجَبَ عَلَيْهِمْ ضَمَانُ مَا أَتْلَفُوهُ بِشَهَادَتِهِمْ
وَلَا يَصِحُ الرُّجُوعُ إِلَّا بِحَضْرَةِ الْحَاكِمِ
وَإِذَا شَهِدَ شَاهِدَانِ بِمَالٍ فَحَكَمَ بِهِ الْحَاكِمُ ثُمَّ رَجَعَا ضَمِنَا لِلْمَشْهُودِ عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْ رَجَعَ أَحَدُهُمَا ضَمِنَ النِّصْفَ
وَإِنْ شَهِدَ بِالْمَالِ ثَلَاثَةٌ فَرَجَعَ أَحَدُهُمْ فَلَا ضَمَانَ عَلَيْهِ فَإِنْ رَجَعَ آخَرُ ضَمِنَ الرَّاجِعَانِ نِصْفَ الْمَالِ
Book of Retraction from Testimony. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him: When the witnesses retract their testimony before the judgment, it is dropped and there is no liability upon them. If judgment was passed based on their testimony, then they retract, the judgment is not overturned, and they are liable for what they caused to be lost by their testimony. Retraction is only valid in the presence of the judge. And if two witnesses testify for property and the judge rules accordingly, then they retract, they compensate the defendant; and if one of them retracts, he compensates half. And if three testify for property and one of them retracts, there is no liability upon him; if another retracts, the two retractors compensate half the property.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof on the subject of retraction of testimony in Hanafi fiqh. The author first presents the matn (core text) containing several rulings: (1) Retraction before judgment: the testimony is void and the witnesses are not liable for any loss, because the judgment has not yet been executed. (2) Retraction after judgment: the judgment stands (it is not overturned) but the witnesses must compensate the party who suffered loss due to their testimony. (3) Retraction is only accepted if it takes place in the presence of the judge. (4) If two witnesses testified for property and after judgment both retract, they must pay the full amount to the defendant; if only one retracts, he pays half. (5) If three witnesses testified for property and one retracts, he pays nothing (still enough testimony from two); if a second retracts, the two retractors together pay half, and the remaining witness's testimony alone is insufficient, so the judgment might be reconsidered? The text says they pay half, implying that the third witness's testimony still supports half? Actually the ruling: when two out of three retract, the two retractors pay half, and presumably the third witness's testimony is not enough to enforce the full amount, so only half is taken? The matn is explicit. The evidence (not included in this literal translation but in the original text) includes hadith, athar, and Quran to support these rulings. The usul principles at the end of each page are also noted.

Key Terms
الرجوع عن الشهادة (al-ruju' 'an al-shahadah): The act of a witness withdrawing his testimony after having given it.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss caused, here specifically arising from false testimony after judgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The judgment is voided and the property is returned.
B) The judgment stands and the witnesses must compensate the defendant.
C) The witnesses are punished for perjury but no compensation.
D) Only one of them is liable if the other proves ignorance.

Key Takeaway
Retraction after judgment does not nullify the verdict; witnesses must compensate the loss they caused.

Retraction of Mixed-Gender Witnesses: Allocating Liability
Ruling on retraction liability with mixed male/female witnesses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when mixed-gender witnesses retract, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Liability for retraction of testimony is apportioned according to the value of each witness's testimony.

This passage from al-Quduri addresses a specific scenario: a man and women testify together in a property case, then some or all retract. The Hanafi school imposes financial liability (daman) on retracting witnesses because their retraction causes loss. However, the school is divided on how to allocate that liability when witnesses are of mixed genders. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the reasoning behind the two positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
For each case (1 man+2 women; 1 man+10 women), state what happens when some or all retract. Note the specific fractions given.
Focus on the pattern: liability mirrors testimony value.
2
Locate the underlying principle
In Hanafi law, a woman's testimony equals half a man's in property matters. Thus, the testimony value of a man is 2 female-units, and each woman is 1 female-unit. Liability is proportional to this value.
This principle is derived from the hadith that witnesses are not weighted by number.
3
Compare the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa divides liability proportionally: the man's share corresponds to his testimony value relative to total. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad divide equally between the male witness and the collective female witnesses, treating the entire group as a single testimony of two men.
The practical difference is significant, e.g., in the 1 man+10 women scenario, the man pays 1/6 vs 1/2.
4
Analyse the proof
The dalil is a mursal hadith that witnesses are not given extra weight by number. This supports treating each woman's testimony as half a man's, but does not directly mandate proportional vs equal division; hence the ikhtilaf.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's equal division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدَ رَجُلٌ وَامْرَأَتَانِ فَرَجَعَتْ امْرَأَةٌ ضَمِنَتْ رُبُعَ الْحَقِّ وَإِنْ رَجَعَتَا ضَمِنَتَا نِصْفَ الْحَقِّ وَإِنْ شَهِدَ رَجُلٌ وَعَشْرُ نِسْوَةٍ فَرَجَعَ ثَمَانٍ فَلَا ضَمَانَ عَلَيْهِنَّ وَفِي رَجَعَتْ أُخْرَى كَانَ عَلَى النِّسْوَةِ رُبُعُ الْحَقِّ فَإِنْ رَجَعَ الرَّجُلُ وَالنِّسَاءُ كَانَ عَلَى الرَّجُلِ سُدُسُ الْحَقِّ وَعَلَى النِّسْوَةِ خَمْسَةُ أَسْدَاسِهِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ: عَلَى الرَّجُلِ النِّصْفُ وَعَلَى النِّسْوَةِ النِّصْفُ
And if a man and two women testify, and one woman retracts, she guarantees a quarter of the right; if both retract, they guarantee half the right. If a man and ten women testify, and eight retract, there is no liability on them; then if another retracts, the women owe a quarter of the right. Then if the man and the women retract, according to Abu Hanifa the man owes one-sixth of the right and the women owe five-sixths. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The man owes half and the women owe half.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri states rulings on retraction of testimony in property cases when witnesses include both men and women. The key principle is that liability is apportioned according to the number of witnesses and their share of testimony. When a lone man and two women testify, each woman's testimony counts as half of a man's. Thus if one woman retracts, she covers one-fourth of the claim (since her testimony was half of the claim's burden). If both retract, they guarantee half. When ten women testify with one man, the man's testimony equals that of two women; so the first eight women who retract cause no liability because the remaining testimony still suffices to establish the claim. Abu Hanifa holds that upon retraction by all, the man's share is one-sixth and the women's share five-sixths, reflecting that each woman's testimony is half of a man's. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani differ, holding that the division is equal (half each) because the original testimony of the man and women is considered collectively as a single testimony from two men, so liability is equally split.

Key Terms
الرجوع عن الشهادة (al-ruju' 'an al-shahadah): Retraction of testimony by a witness after judgment has been passed.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate the loss caused by retraction.
شهادة النساء (shahadat al-nisa'): Testimony of women; in property cases, two women equal one man.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), if a man and ten women testify in a property case and all retract, what fraction of the claim does the man owe?
A) 1/2
B) 1/6
C) 5/6
D) 1/11

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, liability upon retraction of testimony is allocated based on the value of each witness's testimony; a woman's testimony is worth half a man's, leading to different division methods among the founding imams, with the Sahibayn's equal division being the operative position for fatwa.

10 min
Liability for Retraction of Testimony in Marriage and Sale
Rulings on retraction of testimony in marriage and sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on witness liability upon retraction in marriage and sale cases, and apply the benchmarks of mahr al-mithl and qimah al-mithl to determine when compensation is due.

Core Idea
Witnesses are liable only if their false testimony deviates from the proper value causing financial loss.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on retraction of testimony in marriage (nikah) and sale (bay') contracts. The core principle is that liability (daman) is triggered only when the testimony deviates from the proper benchmark—mahr al-mithl for dower and qimah al-mithl for sale price—and causes actual loss. The rulings differ subtly depending on whether the testimony benefits or harms the party.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contexts and their subcases
The passage covers marriage testimony (for the woman and for the man) and sale testimony. For each, there are three subcases: testimony equal to, more than, or less than the benchmark value.
Memorize the pattern: benchmark, above, below.
2
Understand the benchmark values
In marriage, the benchmark is mahr al-mithl (proper dower). In sale, it is qimah al-mithl (fair market value). These represent the objective standard against which loss is measured.
These are customary or expert-determined values.
3
Apply the rule for marriage testimony (woman's side)
When witnesses testify for the woman (i.e., against the man) with a dower equal to or above mahr al-mithl, no liability. If they testify with less than mahr al-mithl, they do not guarantee the deficiency because the woman is deemed to have accepted the lower amount.
No liability for deficiency here because the woman's own claim is for less.
4
Apply the rule for marriage testimony (man's side)
When witnesses testify against the man (i.e., for the woman) with a dower equal to or less than mahr al-mithl, no liability. If they testify with more than mahr al-mithl, they guarantee the excess because the man suffers loss.
Liability only for the excess, not the full dower.
5
Apply the rule for sale testimony
In sale, if witnesses testify to a price equal to or above the fair market value, no liability. If they testify to a price below the fair market value, they guarantee the deficiency when the evidence is established (i.e., when the buyer relies on it).
The phrase 'idha aqamu al-bayyinah' likely means when the plaintiff proves the case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا شَهِدَ شَاهِدَانِ عَلَى الْمَرْأَةِ بِالنِّكَاحِ بِمِقْدَارِ مَهْرِ مِثْلِهَا أَوْ أَكْثَرَ ثُمَّ رَجَعَا فَلَا ضَمَانَ عَلَيْهِمَا وَإِنْ شَهِدَا بِأَقَلَّ مِنْ مَهْرِ الْمِثْلِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَا لَمْ يَضْمَنَا التَّقْصَانَ وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا شَهِدَا عَلَى رَجُلٍ بِتَزْوِيجِ امْرَأَةٍ بِمِقْدَارٍ مَهْرِ مِثْلِهَا أَوْ أَقَلَّ ثُمَّ رَجَعَا لَمْ يَضْمَنَا الْوَإِنْ شَهِدَا بِأَكْثَرَ مِنْ مَهْرِ الْمِثْلِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَا ضَمِنَا الزَّيَادَةَ وَإِنْ شَهِدَا بِبَيْعِ مِثْلِ الْقِيمَةِ أَوْ أَكْثَرَ ثُمَّ رَجَعَا لَمْ يَضْمَنَا وَإِنْ شَهِدَا بِأَقَلَّ مِنْ الْقِيمَةِ ضَمِنَا النُّقْصَانَ إِذَا أَقَامُوا الْبَيِّنَةَ
And if two witnesses testify against a woman concerning marriage with a dower equal to her proper dower or more, then they retract, there is no liability upon them. If they testify with less than the proper dower, then retract, they do not guarantee the deficiency. Likewise, if they testify against a man that he married a woman with a dower equal to her proper dower or less, then retract, they do not guarantee anything. And if they testify with more than the proper dower, then retract, they guarantee the excess. And if they testify concerning a sale for the equivalent of the fair price or more, then retract, they do not guarantee. And if they testify with less than the fair price, they guarantee the deficiency, if they establish the evidence (or when the evidence is established).
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage addresses retraction of testimony in marriage (nikah) and sale (bay') contracts. The underlying principle is that the worth of a woman in marriage is determined by her proper dower (mahr al-mithl), and the worth of goods by their fair market value (qimah al-mithl). If witnesses testify to a dower equal to or higher than the proper dower, their testimony does not cause loss to the woman (since she gets at least her due). If they testify to a lower dower, the deficiency is not recoverable because the judgment is based on their testimony, and the loss is attributed to the woman's own action (she accepted the lower dower). Conversely, if witnesses testify to a dower higher than the proper dower against a man, they cause him loss and must pay the excess. In sales, similar logic applies: testifying to a price equal to or higher than the market value causes no loss to the seller; testifying to a lower price causes loss to the seller, so the witnesses guarantee the deficiency. The phrase 'idha aqamu al-bayyinah' likely means 'when they (the plaintiffs) establish the proof' or could be a scribal note.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower: an amount appropriate for a woman of similar status, family, and circumstances.
قيمة المثل (qimah al-mithl): The fair market value of the sold item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two witnesses testify that a woman's dower is 400 dirhams, but her mahr al-mithl is 600 dirhams. They retract after judgment. What is their liability?
A) They must pay the deficiency of 200 dirhams.
B) They must pay the full 600 dirhams.
C) They owe nothing.
D) They must pay the woman 200 dirhams and the man 400 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, witness liability upon retraction depends on whether the testimony deviated from the proper value and caused actual financial loss; not every false testimony triggers compensation.

Retraction in Talaq, Itq, and Qisas
Rulings on retraction in talaq, itq, qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on liability of witnesses who retract after their testimony causes judgment in divorce, manumission, and retaliation cases.

Core Idea
Witnesses must compensate financial loss caused by retraction, but no liability if no harm occurs.

The law holds witnesses accountable for the consequences of their testimony. When they retract after judgment, the key factor is whether their testimony directly caused a financial loss. In this lesson, we explore three distinct cases from al-Quduri: divorce before and after consummation, manumission, and retaliation. Understanding the underlying principle—loss causation—will enable you to predict liability in similar situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling for each case
For each scenario (divorce before consummation, after consummation, manumission, qisas), state the specific ruling on liability upon retraction. Note the hukm level: in all cases where loss occurs, guarantee (daman) is wajib.
2
Trace the loss causation
Determine what financial loss, if any, resulted from the retraction. In divorce before consummation, half dower is lost; after consummation, no loss because full dower is already due. In manumission, the slave's value is lost. In qisas, the blood money (diyah) is owed because execution is irreversible.
Loss must be directly attributable to the testimony.
3
Analyze the exception in qisas
Why are the witnesses not executed (qisas) even though their testimony led to death? The Hanafi view holds that their act is not direct killing; the execution was carried out by the state based on their testimony. Therefore, diyah suffices.
Analogous to accidental killing (qatl al-khata').
4
Connect to the dalil
The Quranic verse on diyah for accidental killing (4:92) provides the basis for treating the witnesses' retraction like involuntary homicide, warranting diyah not qisas.
Qiyas is used.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Some schools may hold that witnesses in qisas are executed (qisas) because their testimony was the cause. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدَا عَلَى رَجُلٍ أَنَّهُ طَلَّقَ امْرَأَتَهُ قَبْلَ الدُّخُولِ بِمَا ثُمَّ رَجَعَا ضَمِنَا نِصْفَ الْمَهْرِ وَإِنْ كَانَ بَعْدَ الدُّخُولِ لَمْ يَضْمَنَا وَإِنْ شَهِدَا أَنَّهُ أَعْتَقَ عَبْدَهُ ثُمَّ رَجَعَا ضَمِنَا قِيمَتَهُ ١٣ وَإِنْ شَهِدَا بِقِصَاصٍ ثُمَّ رَجَعَا بَعْدَ الْقَتْلِ ضَمِنَا الدِّيَةَ وَلَا يُقْتَصُّ مِنْهُمَا هَا وَإِذَا رَجَعَ شُهُودُ الْفَرْع ضَمِنُوا وَإِنْ رَجَعَ شُهُودُ الْأَصْلِ وَقَالُوا: لَمَّ نُشْهِدْ شُهُودَ الْفَرْعِ عَلَى شَهَادَتِنَا فَلَا ضَمَانَ عَلَيْهِمْ وَإِنْ قَالُوا: أَشْهَدْنَاهُمْ وَغَلِطْنَا ضَمِنُوا ١٦ وَإِنْ قَالَ شُهُودُ الْفَرْعِ: كَذَبَ شُهُودُ الْأَصْلِ أَوْ غَلِطُوا فِي شَهَادَتِهِمْ ثُمَّ يُلْتَفَتْ إِلَى ذَلِكَ
And if they (two witnesses) testify against a man that he divorced his wife before consummation, then they retract, they guarantee half the dower. If it was after consummation, they do not guarantee. And if they testify that he emancipated his slave, then retract, they guarantee his value. And if they testify to a case of retaliation (qisas) and then retract after execution, they guarantee the blood money (diyah), and they are not subjected to retaliation. And when the subsidiary witnesses (shuhud al-far') retract, they guarantee. If the original witnesses (shuhud al-asl) retract and say: 'We did not cause the subsidiary witnesses to testify based on our testimony,' then there is no liability on them. If they say: 'We made them testify and we were mistaken,' they guarantee. And if the subsidiary witnesses say: 'The original witnesses lied or were mistaken in their testimony,' then this is considered.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage covers several distinct cases: 

1) Divorce (talaq): If witnesses testify that a man divorced his wife before consummation, and then retract, they must pay half the dower because the wife loses half her dower (since post-divorce before consummation, half is due). But if after consummation, no loss occurs because she already receives full dower, so no liability. 

2) Emancipation (itq): If witnesses testify that a man freed his slave, causing the man to lose the slave's value, upon retraction they guarantee the slave's value. 

3) Retaliation (qisas): If witnesses testify in a homicide case leading to execution, and then retract after execution, they must pay the diyah (blood money) because the execution is irreversible, but they are not executed themselves (since qisas cannot be applied to them as they did not kill directly). 

4) Subsidiary witnesses (shuhud al-far'): When witnesses testify based on original witnesses (tazkiyah), if the subsidiary witnesses retract, they are liable because their testimony caused the judgment. If the original witnesses retract and claim they did not direct the subsidiaries to testify, they are not liable. If they admit they instructed them but were mistaken, they are liable. If the subsidiaries accuse the originals of lying or error, the court will investigate that claim.

Key Terms
شهود (shuhud): Witnesses in a legal proceeding.
دية (diyah): Blood money paid to the victim's family in homicide or injury cases.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation, i.e., taking a life for a life or injury for injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two witnesses testify that a man divorced his wife before consummation, then retract. What do they owe?
A) Full dower
B) Half dower
C) Nothing
D) Mahr al-mithl

Key Takeaway
Witnesses must compensate the financial loss directly caused by their retracted testimony, but no liability exists if no loss occurred.

Retraction of Subsidiary Witnesses (Shuhud al-Far')
Rulings on retraction of subsidiary and original witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the liability of original and subsidiary witnesses upon retraction and identify when each is liable.

Core Idea
Subsidiary witnesses are liable upon retraction; original witnesses are liable only if they knowingly caused the subsidiaries to testify.

In Islamic legal procedure, witnesses may testify based on the testimony of other witnesses (subsidiary testimony). When retraction occurs, the liability differs depending on whether the subsidiariess acted on their own or were directed. This lesson examines the nuanced rules governing original and subsidiary witnesses in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties: original and subsidiary witnesses
Original witnesses (shuhud al-asl) directly witnessed the event. Subsidiary witnesses (shuhud al-far') testify based on the originals' testimony, often after the originals have been deemed reliable.
The subsidiary's testimony is derivative.
2
Rule for subsidiary witnesses retracting
If the subsidiary witnesses retract, they are liable (daman) because their testimony directly caused the judgment.
They are the proximate cause.
3
Rule for original witnesses retracting: two scenarios
If originals retract and claim they did not direct the subsidiaries, they are not liable. If they admit they directed them but were mistaken, they are liable.
Liability hinges on causation and intent.
4
Rule when subsidiaries accuse originals of lying
If subsidiary witnesses say the originals lied or were mistaken, the court will investigate that claim. If proven, the subsidiaries may be excused.
This shifts the blame back to originals.
5
Understand the underlying principle
Liability follows causation: whoever is the nearest cause of the judgment bears the loss, unless they acted under a misapprehension caused by the other party.
Similar to tort law principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if they (two witnesses) testify against a man that he divorced his wife before consummation, then they retract, they guarantee half the dower. If it was after consummation, they do not guarantee. And if they testify that he emancipated his slave, then retract, they guarantee his value. And if they testify to a case of retaliation (qisas) and then retract after execution, they guarantee the blood money (diyah), and they are not subjected to retaliation. And when the subsidiary witnesses (shuhud al-far') retract, they guarantee. If the original witnesses (shuhud al-asl) retract and say: 'We did not cause the subsidiary witnesses to testify based on our testimony,' then there is no liability on them. If they say: 'We made them testify and we were mistaken,' they guarantee. And if the subsidiary witnesses say: 'The original witnesses lied or were mistaken in their testimony,' then this is considered.
