Commentary
This passage covers several distinct cases: 

1) Divorce (talaq): If witnesses testify that a man divorced his wife before consummation, and then retract, they must pay half the dower because the wife loses half her dower (since post-divorce before consummation, half is due). But if after consummation, no loss occurs because she already receives full dower, so no liability.

If the original witnesses retract and claim they did not direct the subsidiaries to testify, they are not liable. If they admit they instructed them but were mistaken, they are liable. If the subsidiaries accuse the originals of lying or error, the court will investigate that claim.

Key Terms
شهود الفرع (shuhud al-far'): Subsidiary witnesses who testify based on the testimony of original witnesses (shuhud al-asl).
شهود الأصل (shuhud al-asl): Original witnesses who directly witnessed the event and testified before the court or directed others to testify.

Retraction of Testimony in Divorce Cases
Ruling on retraction of divorce testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on witness retraction in divorce and apply the condition (consummation) that determines liability.

Core Idea
Witness retraction only triggers compensation if it caused actual financial loss.

In the Book of Retraction of Testimony, the author presents a key distinction: when witnesses withdraw their testimony about a divorce, their liability depends on whether the divorce occurred before or after consummation. This ruling illustrates how the Hanafi school ties legal consequences to actual financial harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is retraction of testimony about divorce. The ruling distinguishes two scenarios based on timing of divorce.
2
Note the two scenarios
Scenario 1: divorce before consummation. Scenario 2: divorce after consummation.
3
State the consequence for each
Before consummation: witnesses guarantee half the mahr. After consummation: no guarantee.
4
Understand the underlying principle
Liability arises only if retraction caused financial loss. After consummation, full mahr is already owed, so no loss.
The Urdu principle explains that the right to the vulva is valued at marriage but not at divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الرُّجُوعِ عَنْ الشَّهَادَةِ وَإِنْ شَهِدَا عَلَى رَجُلٍ أَنَّهُ طَلَّقَ امْرَأَتَهُ قَبْلَ الدُّخُولِ بِمَا ثُمَّ رَجَعَا ضَمِنَا نِصْفَ الْمَهْرِ وَإِنْ كَانَ بَعْدَ الدُّخُولِ لَمْ يَضْمَنَا اصول: نکاح کے وقت بضع کی قیمت اسکی عزت بڑھانے کے لئے لگائی جاتی ہے اور طلاق کے وقت اسکی کوئی قیمت نہیں ہوتی، لہذا ضمان نہیں ہو گا۔
Book of Retraction of Testimony. And if two witnesses testify that a man divorced his wife before consummation with her, then they retract, they guarantee half the dower. And if it was after consummation, they do not guarantee. Principle: At the time of marriage, the value of the vulva is set to increase her honor, and at the time of divorce it has no value, so there is no guarantee.

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Retraction of Testimony with a ruling: when two witnesses testify to a divorce before consummation and then retract, they must pay half the mahr because their testimony caused the wife to lose her right to that half. After consummation, the full mahr is already obligated, so retraction does not cause any loss. The Urdu principle explains that the right to the vulva is valued at marriage but not at divorce, so no guarantee.

Key Terms
شهدا (shahida): Two witnesses who testify in a legal case.
الرجوع عن الشهادة (al-ruju' 'an al-shahadah): The act of withdrawing one's testimony after it has been given and acted upon.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss caused by retraction.

Key Takeaway
The liability of retracting witnesses depends on whether their testimony caused actual financial loss; after consummation, no loss arises because full mahr is already due.

Retraction in Emancipation and Under-Valuation
Ruling on retraction of testimony regarding freeing a slave or undervaluing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on witness retraction in emancipation and under-valuation cases, and explain how the Quranic verse on qisas serves as the proof.

Core Idea
A retracting witness compensates the loss caused—full value for false freedom, deficiency for under-valuation.

This passage from Al-Quduri presents two scenarios of witness retraction involving a slave. The first ruling addresses witnesses who testify that a master freed his slave, then retract—their testimony caused the master to lose his property entirely. The second ruling addresses witnesses who undervalue the slave, causing only a partial loss. The ruling is grounded in a universal principle derived from the Quranic law of qisas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the source carefully: witnesses retracting from testimony of emancipation pay full value; witnesses who testified to a lower value pay only the difference (deficiency).
The word 'qimah' means full market value; 'nuqsan' means the shortfall.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 5:45 (the qisas verse) as the proof. Note that the verse establishes a principle of equivalence in compensation.
The verse is cited as 'wajh' (a face of the proof), indicating it is used by analogy.
3
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
The verse states that life for life, eye for eye, etc., implies that any loss caused must be compensated fully. By analogy, witnesses who cause loss through retraction must compensate—full value for total loss, deficiency for partial loss.
This is a qiyas from the general principle of 'la darar wa la dirar'.
4
Note the authority level
The ruling is from the matn of Al-Quduri, which is part of Zahir al-Riwayah, and is mufta bihi without known intra-Hanafi disagreement.
Other schools may require a more explicit textual proof, but Hanafis rely on the general import of the verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدَا أَنَّهُ أَعْتَقَ عَبْدَهُ ثُمَّ رَجَعَا ضَمِنَا قِيمَتَهُ وَإِنْ شَهِدَا بِأَقَلَّ مِنْ الْقِيمَةِ ضَمِنَا النُّقْصَانَا وجه (۲) الآية لثبوت ذَلِكَ: وَكَتَبْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ فِيهَا أَنَّ النَّفْسَ بِالنَّفْسِ وَالْعَيْنَ بِالْعَيْنِ وَالْأَنفَ بِالْأَنفِ وَالْأُذُنَ بِالْأُذُنِ وَالسِّنَّ بِالسِّينَ وَالْجُرُوحَ قِصَاصٌ فَمَن تَصَدَّقَ بِهِ فَهُوَ كَفَّارَةٌ لَّهُ وَمَن لَّمْ يَحْكُم بِمَا أَنزَلَ اللَّهُ فَأَوْلَتَبِكَ هُمُ الظَّالِمُونَ ) (سورة المائدة، 5 أيت، نمبر (45)
And if they testify that he freed his slave, then they retract, they guarantee his value. And if they testify to less than the value, they guarantee the deficiency. Proof (Wajh 2 from the Quran) for that: 'And We prescribed for them therein: a life for a life, an eye for an eye, a nose for a nose, an ear for an ear, a tooth for a tooth, and for wounds is legal retribution. But whoever gives charity for it, it is an expiation for him. And whoever does not judge by what Allah has revealed, then it is those who are the wrongdoers.' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:45)
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage gives two rulings on retraction in cases involving slaves. First, if witnesses testify that a master freed his slave, then retract, they must pay the slave's full value because their testimony deprived the master of his property. Second, if they testify that the slave's value is less than the actual value, they guarantee only the difference. The proof from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:45) is cited: the verse establishes that causing loss requires compensation, whether the loss is total (like a life or an eye) or partial. Here, the witnesses caused loss by their false testimony.

Key Terms
عتق (itq): Emancipation of a slave by the owner's declaration.
قيمة (qimah): Market value of the slave at the time of testimony.
نقصان (nuqsan): The difference between the actual value and the testified lower value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two witnesses testify that a slave is worth 500 dirhams, but the actual value is 1000. They then retract. What do they owe?
A) 1000 dirhams
B) 500 dirhams
C) Nothing
D) 250 dirhams

Key Takeaway
Witnesses who retract must compensate the loss they caused—full value for false freedom, deficiency for undervaluation.

Retraction in Qisas: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Ruling on retraction after qisas execution with proof and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on retraction in qisas cases and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position by identifying the key factor of intent (error vs. intention).

Core Idea
Witnesses who mistakenly cause execution pay diyah, not qisas, because compensation follows error.

When witnesses retract after a qisas execution, the question arises: are they liable to qisas or only financial compensation? This lesson dissects the Hanafi position—diyah—contrasted with the Shafi'i view that could impose qisas. The decisive factor is the witnesses' intent: error (khat') versus deliberate falsehood ('amd).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify what the Hanafi school holds for witnesses who retract after qisas execution: they pay diyah, not qisas.
The ruling applies regardless of whether the retraction is before or after execution, but the text specifically addresses post-execution retraction.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Examine the two proofs: Quran 4:92 (diyah for accidental killing) and the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that witnesses in an error case owe diyah.
The Quranic verse is used by analogy—the witnesses caused death through error, so diyah is appropriate.
3
Identify the Shafi'i counter-position
State the Shafi'i view based on al-Hasan al-Basri: a witness who intentionally testified to cause execution is subject to qisas if he retracts.
The Shafi'i proof relies on the element of intent, not error.
4
Follow the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafi school reconciles the two: the Shafi'i case applies only when the witness admits intentional falsehood; the Hanafi ruling is for error.
This resolution shows that the two positions are not contradictory but apply to different scenarios.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Realize the practical difference: if witnesses claim mistake, Hanafi imposes diyah; if they admit intent, Shafi'i would apply qisas.
In fatwa, the Hanafi school generally presumes error unless proven otherwise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدَا بِقِصَاصٍ ثُمَّ رَجَعَا بَعْدَ الْقَتْلِ ضَمِنَا الدِّيَةَ وَلَا يُقْتَصُّ مِنْهُمَا وجه (۱) الآية لثبوت ذَلِكَ: (وَمَن قَتَلَ مُؤْمِنًا خَطَئًا فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مُّؤْمِنَةٍ وَدِيَةٌ مُسَلَّمَةٌ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ) (سورة النساء، 4 أيت، نمبر 92) وجه:(۲) قول التابعي لثبوت ذَلِكَ: عن إبراهيم أنه قال: إذا شهد شاهدان على قطع يد رجل فقضى القاضي بذلك ثم رجعا عن شهادتهما أن عليهما الدية، وإن رجع أحدهما فعليه نصف دية اليد وبهذا كان يأخذ أبو حنيفة وأبو يوسف ومحمد، (الاصل لمحمد بن الحسن، باب الرجوع عن الشهادة في الحدود نمبر46) وجه (۱) دليل الشافعى قول التابعى لثبوت خلاف ذلك: عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، قَالَ: " إِذَا شَهِدَ شَاهِدَانِ عَلَى قَتْلِ، ثُمَّ قُتِلَ الْقَاتِلُ، ثُمَّ يَرْجِعُ أَحَدُ الشَّاهِدِينَ قُتِلَ ". قَالَ الشَّيْخُ: " وَهَذَا فِيهِ إِذَا قَالَ: عَمِدْتُ أَنْ أَشْهَدَ عَلَيْهِ لِيُقْتَلَ، وَالْأَوَّلُ فِي الْخَطَأَ"، (السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ : الرُّجُوعُ عَنِ الشَّهَادَةِ، نمبر 21193)
And if they testify to qisas, then retract after the execution, they guarantee the diyah, and qisas is not executed upon them. Proof (Wajh 1 from Quran): 'And whoever kills a believer by mistake, then freeing a believing slave and a compensation (diyah) delivered to his family' (Surah an-Nisa 4:92). Proof (Wajh 2 from a tabi'i): from Ibrahim, he said: If two witnesses testify to cutting off a man's hand, and the judge rules accordingly, then they retract, they owe the diyah; if one retracts, he owes half the diyah of the hand. This was the view of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. (Al-Asl of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, Bab al-Ruju' an al-Shahadah fi al-Hudud #46). Proof (Wajh 1) of the Shafi'i evidence from a tabi'i: from al-Hasan, he said: If two witnesses testify to a killing, then the killer is executed, then one of the witnesses retracts, he is killed. The author (al-Shaykh) said: This applies when he said 'I intentionally testified to have him killed,' and the first (Hanafi view) is in case of error. (Al-Sunan al-Kubra li al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Ruju' an al-Shahadah #21193).
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on retraction of testimony in qisas cases. If two witnesses cause the execution of a person through their testimony and then retract, they are not executed themselves (qisas) but must pay diyah (blood money). The proof is from Quran 4:92 (diyah for accidental killing) and from a saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (a tabi'i) that the Hanafi imams adopted. Then the Shafi'i view is presented: if a witness intentionally and falsely testified to cause death, and then retracts after execution, he is subject to qisas. The Hanafi response, attributed to 'al-Shaykh', distinguishes error (khat') from intent ('amd). The Hanafi ruling here is for the case of error (the witnesses made a mistake, not deliberately lied). Thus, the liability is financial, not capital. The passage thus resolves the inter-madhhab dispute by reconciling the two positions based on intent.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment (life for life, limb for limb).
دية (diyah): Blood money paid to the victim's family in compensation for wrongful death.
خطأ (khat'): Error; unintentional mistake.
عمد ('amd): Intentional; deliberate action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if two witnesses mistakenly testify to a murder, leading to execution, and then retract, what do they owe?
A) Nothing
B) Qisas
C) Diyah
D) Half the diyah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school imposes diyah, not qisas, on witnesses who retract after a qisas execution, based on the Quranic rule for accidental killing and the distinction between error and intent.

Liability on Retraction of Branch and Original Witnesses
Rulings on liability when branch or original witnesses retract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the liability rules when branch or original witnesses retract in Hanafi fiqh and apply them to given scenarios.

Core Idea
Liability follows the testimony that directly affected the ruling: branch witnesses, unless original witnesses admit error.

Testimony in Islamic courts can be delegated through branch witnesses. When retraction occurs, who bears the financial liability depends on whether the original witnesses admit appointment or deny it. This lesson parses the scenarios from the Quduri text to clarify the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Distinguish between original witnesses (shuhud al-asl) and branch witnesses (shuhud al-far'). Branch witnesses testify based on the original witnesses' testimony.
2
Scenario: Branch witnesses retract
If branch witnesses retract their testimony, they alone are liable (daman) because their testimony directly affected the court's ruling.
The branch witnesses' retraction is decisive.
3
Scenario: Original witnesses retract and deny appointment
If original witnesses retract and claim they never appointed the branch witnesses, they are not liable. The branch witnesses are liable since they testified without authorization.
Denial of appointment removes liability from originals.
4
Scenario: Original witnesses admit appointment but claim mistake
If original witnesses say 'We appointed them and we were mistaken,' they become liable. The branch witnesses are not liable because the originals acknowledge error.
Admission of mistake shifts liability to originals.
5
Scenario: Branch witnesses accuse originals of lying or error
If branch witnesses claim the originals lied or erred, the court will investigate (yultafat). Liability depends on findings.
The court must verify the claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا رَجَعَ شُهُودُ الْفَرْع ضَمِنُوا وَإِنْ رَجَعَ شُهُودُ الْأَصْلِ وَقَالُوا: لَمَّ نُشْهِدْ شُهُودَ الْفَرْعِ عَلَى شَهَادَتِنَا فَلَا ضَمَانَ عَلَيْهِمْ وَإِنْ قَالُوا: أَشْهَدْنَاهُمْ وَغَلِطْنَا ضَمِنُوا وَإِنْ قَالَ شُهُودُ الْفَرْعِ: كَذَبَ شُهُودُ الْأَصْلِ أَوْ غَلِطُوا فِي شَهَادَقِهِمْ ثُمَّ يُلْتَفَتْ إِلَى ذَلِكَ اصول: مجلس قضا میں فرع گواہی دیگر رجوع کیا تو فرع ہی ضامن ہو گا کیونکہ فرع کی گواہی ہی بنیاد ہے۔
And if the branch witnesses retract, they guarantee. And if the original witnesses retract and say: 'We did not appoint the branch witnesses to testify on our testimony,' then there is no liability upon them. And if they say: 'We appointed them and we were mistaken,' they guarantee. And if the branch witnesses say: 'The original witnesses lied or erred in their testimony,' then that is considered. Principle: In the court, if the branch witness retracts his testimony, then he is the guarantor, because his testimony is the foundation.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage clarifies liability when testimony is given through branch witnesses (shuhud al-far') who testify on the basis of the original witnesses' (shuhud al-asl) testimony. If the branch witnesses retract, they are liable because their testimony directly affected the ruling. If the original witnesses retract and deny having appointed the branch witnesses, they are not liable because the branch witnesses acted without authorization. However, if the original witnesses admit they appointed the branch but claim they were mistaken in their original testimony, then they are liable. If the branch witnesses accuse the original of lying or error, the court will investigate and act accordingly. The Urdu principle emphasizes that the branch witnesses' testimony is the direct cause, so they are liable upon retraction.

Key Terms
شهود الفرع (shuhud al-far'): Secondary witnesses who testify on the basis of the testimony of original witnesses (shuhud al-asl).
شهود الأصل (shuhud al-asl): Primary witnesses who personally observed the event and may delegate branch witnesses to testify.
ضمان (daman): Financial liability for loss caused by retraction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If original witnesses retract and claim they never appointed the branch witnesses, what is the ruling?
A) Original witnesses are liable.
B) Branch witnesses are liable.
C) Both are liable.
D) No one is liable.

Key Takeaway
Liability for retracted testimony in Hanafi fiqh depends on whether original witnesses admit or deny appointment: denial exonerates them, admission with error makes them liable; branch witnesses are liable when they retract or when originals deny appointment.

Retraction of Ihsan Witnesses in Zina Cases
Ruling when witnesses to ihsan retract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when ihsan witnesses retract and explain why they bear no liability.

Core Idea
Ihsan witnesses do not guarantee anything upon retraction because their testimony is secondary.

Testimony in hudud cases is subject to strict rules, especially regarding retraction. This lesson examines a specific scenario where two witnesses to ihsan (the preterite condition that escalates the punishment to stoning) retract. The ruling provides clarity on when witnesses are liable for compensation and when they are not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties involved
The scenario involves four witnesses testifying to zina (the act) and two witnesses testifying to ihsan (the preterite condition). The ihsan witnesses retract.
2
Distinguish the roles of the testimonies
The zina testimony directly proves the act of zina, while the ihsan testimony only proves the condition that turns the punishment from lashing to stoning. The punishment is primarily based on the zina testimony.
If the zina witnesses retract, they would be liable, but that is not covered here.
3
State the ruling on retraction
According to the text: 'If the witnesses to ihsan retract, they do not guarantee anything.' They are not liable for any compensation.
The ruling applies even if the retraction occurs after the punishment has been carried out.
4
Explain the legal reasoning
The ihsan testimony is secondary; it does not directly cause the punishment. Therefore, retraction does not create liability. This is a specific Hanafi rule in the law of testimony.
This distinguishes ihsan witnesses from zina witnesses, who are directly causative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدَ أَرْبَعَةٌ بِالزَّنَا وَشَاهِدَانِ بِالْإِحْصَانِ فَرَجَعَ شُهُودُ الْإِحْصَانِ لَمْ يَضْمَنُوا
And if four witnesses testify to zina and two witnesses to ihsan (preterite/marriage), then if the witnesses to ihsan retract, they do not guarantee anything.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling on retraction in a case of zina (adultery/fornication) where four witnesses are required to prove the act, and two additional witnesses are needed to prove ihsan (that the offender was previously married) to impose the stoning penalty. If the ihsan witnesses retract, they are not liable for any compensation because their testimony did not cause the punishment directly; the punishment depends primarily on the zina testimony. The zina witnesses themselves are not mentioned here, but if they retract, they would face liability (perhaps qisas if the punishment was already executed).

Key Terms
إحصان (ihsan): Legal status of being previously married, which makes the zina punishment stoning instead of lashing.
زنا (zina): Unlawful sexual intercourse between a man and a woman not married to each other.
شهود الإحصان (shuhud al-ihsan): Witnesses who testify to the condition of ihsan (preterite marriage) in a zina case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the two witnesses to ihsan retract after the punishment has been carried out, what is the ruling according to this passage?
A) They must pay diyah.
B) They are subject to qisas.
C) They do not guarantee anything.
D) Their retraction is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Ihsan witnesses bear no liability upon retraction because their testimony is secondary to the zina testimony.

Retraction of Tazkiyah and Oath/Condition Witnesses
Rulings on retraction of character witnesses and oath/condition testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on liability when tazkiyah witnesses retract and when witnesses to oath and condition retract, and apply the principle that liability follows the effective cause.

Core Idea
Liability for retraction follows the effective cause (illa), not the mere condition (shart).

In Hanafi testimony law, retraction of witnesses can lead to financial liability. This lesson examines two specific cases: retraction of character witnesses (tazkiyah) and retraction of witnesses testifying to an oath or a condition. The key distinction is that the oath is the effective cause of the legal action, while the condition is merely a prerequisite; thus liability attaches solely to the witnesses of the cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling
Find the statement: 'If the tazkiyah witnesses retract their recommendation, they guarantee.' Recognize that tazkiyah witnesses endorse a witness's uprightness; their retraction triggers liability for any loss caused.
The hukm is that they must compensate (daman).
2
Identify the second ruling
Find the statement about two witnesses to an oath and two to a condition. The ruling: if all retract, only the oath witnesses are liable.
3
Understand the legal principle
The Urdu principle explains: the oath is the effective cause ('illa) of the legal action, while the condition is merely a condition (shart). The ruling is built on the cause, not the condition.
This is a Hanafi usul principle applied to testimony.
4
Apply the principle to the scenario
In a combined case, even though both sets of witnesses retract, only the witnesses to the cause (oath) bear liability because the action depends on the oath, not the condition.
If the condition were also a cause, liability would be shared.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا رَجَعَ الْمُزَكُونَ عَنْ التَّرْكِيَةِ ضَمِنُوا وَإِذَا شَهِدَ شَاهِدَانِ بِالْيَمِينِ وَشَاهِدَانِ بِوُجُودِ الشَّرْطِ ثُمَّ رَجَعُوا فَالضَّمَانُ عَلَى شُهُودِ الْيَمِينِ خَاصَّةً اصول قسم کھانا یہ کام کی اصل علت ہے، اور شرط تو بس ایک شرط ہے، اس پر کام کا مدار نہیں ہے۔
And if the tazkiyah witnesses retract their recommendation, they guarantee. And if two witnesses testify to the oath and two witnesses to the existence of the condition, then they retract, the liability is specifically on the witnesses to the oath. Principle: Swearing the oath is the effective cause of the action, while the condition is merely a condition; the action does not turn upon it.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage gives two rulings. First, witnesses who have given tazkiyah (character endorsement) for a witness and then retract are liable because their endorsement allowed the witness's testimony to be accepted, potentially causing loss. Second, in cases involving an oath (yamin) and a condition (shart), the witness to the oath is solely liable if both retract, because the oath is the effective cause (`illa) of the legal action. The Urdu principle explains that the oath is the fundamental cause, while the condition is just a prerequisite; thus the liability attaches to the cause.

Key Terms
مزكون (muzakkun): Witnesses who testify to the uprightness (tazkiyah) of other witnesses.
تزكية (tazkiyah): The process of attesting to the reliability and uprightness of a witness.
يمين (yamin): Oath sworn by a party to establish a right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If witnesses to both the oath and the condition retract, who is liable according to the Hanafi school?
A) Both sets of witnesses equally.
B) The condition witnesses only.
C) The oath witnesses only.
D) Neither set.

Key Takeaway
Liability for retraction of witnesses hinges on whether their testimony pertains to the effective cause (illa) or a mere condition (shart); only the cause matters.

Acceptance of a Fasiq's Testimony: The Hanafi Distinction
Ruling with proofs on fasiq testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting a fasiq's testimony in mu'amalat vs diyanat and identify the three proofs that support this distinction.

Core Idea
A fasiq's testimony is accepted in transactions but not in religious matters — the ruling is rooted in the Quranic exception for repentance and the practice of Umar.

This passage from Quduri establishes a crucial distinction in Hanafi testimony law: the acceptance of a fasiq's word depends on context. In transactional matters, a fasiq's testimony can be accepted, but in religious reports, only an 'adl is acceptable. The author provides three pieces of evidence, demonstrating the Hanafi method of combining nass (Quran) and practice (Sunnah/qawl sahabi).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two-part ruling
Recognize that the passage first states acceptance in mu'amalat then rejection in diyanat.
2
List the three proofs
Note the two Quranic verses and the practice of Umar cited in the text.
3
Analyze the first proof (Surah al-Nur)
Explain how the exception for repentance implies acceptance in civil matters.
This is the most explicit dalil.
4
Examine the proof from Umar's actions
Show how Umar accepted testimony of repentant slanderers, confirming the ruling.
5
Consider the cross-madhhab difference
Briefly contrast with Shafi'i absolute rejection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَقْبَلُ فِي الْمُعَامَلَاتِ قَوْلَ الْفَاسِقِ وَلَا يَقْبَلُ فِي أَخْبَارِ الدِّيَانَاتِ إِلَّا الْعَدْلَ

وجْه : (1) الآية لثبوت وَيَقْبَلُ فِي الْمُعَامَلَاتِ قَوْلَ الْفَاسِقِ \ ﴿ فَاجْتَنِبُوا الرِّجْسَ مِنَ الْأَوْثَنِ وَاجْتَنِبُوا قَوْلَ النُّورِ ﴾ (سورة الحج، 22 آيت نمبر 30)
وجْه : (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيَقْبَلُ فِي الْمُعَامَلَاتِ قَوْلَ الْفَاسِقِ \ وَجَلَدَ عُمَرُ أَبَا بَكْرَةَ وَشِبْلَ بْنَ مَعْبَدٍ وَنَافِعًا بِقَذْفِ الْمُغِيرَةِ ثُمَّ اسْتَتَابَهُمْ وَقَالَ مَنْ تَابَ قَبِلْتُ شَهَادَتَهُ وَأَجَازَهُ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ عُتْبَةَ وَعُمَرُ بْنُ عَبْدِ الْعَزِيزِ وَسَعِيدُ بْنُ جُبَيْرٍ وَطَاوُسٌ وَمُجَاهِدٌ وَالشَّعْيُّ وَعِكْرِمَةُ وَالزُّهْرِيُّ وَمُحَارِبُ بْنُ دِثَارٍ وَشُرَيْحٌ وَمُعَاوِيَةُ بْنُ قُرَّةَ»» (صحيح البخاري، شَهَادَةِ الْقَاذِفِ وَالسَّارِقِ وَالزَّانِي، غمبر 2648)
وجْه : (۳) الآية لثبوت وَيَقْبَلُ فِي الْمُعَامَلَاتِ قَوْلَ الْفَاسِقِ \ ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ ثُمَّ لَمْ يَأْتُواْ بِأَرْبَعَةِ شُهَدَاءَ فَاجْلِدُوهُمْ ثَمَنِينَ جَلْدَةً وَلَا تَقْبَلُوا لَهُمْ شَهَادَةً أَبَدِّأْ وَأُوْلَبِكَ هُمُ الْفَاسِقُونَ إِلَّا الَّذِينَ تَابُوا مِنْ بَعْدِ ذَلِكَ وَأَصْلَحُوا فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ غَفُورٌ رَّحِيمٌ﴾ (سورة النور، 24 أيت، نمبر 5/4) ١٨
اصول: معاملات میں فاسقوں کی شہادت مقبول ہو گی، البتہ دیانت میں فاسقوں کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی
And he accepts in transactions the statement of the sinful person, and he does not accept in matters of religion except the just person. Evidence: (1) The verse for establishing: 'So avoid the filth of idols and avoid false speech' (Surah al-Hajj, 22:30). Evidence: (2) The saying of a companion for establishing: 'Umar flogged Abu Bakrah, Shibl ibn Ma'bad, and Nafi' for slandering al-Mughirah, then he sought repentance from them and said: Whoever repents, I accept his testimony. And this was permitted by Abdullah ibn Utbah, Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, Sa'id ibn Jubayr, Tawus, Mujahid, al-Sha'bi, Ikrimah, al-Zuhri, Muharib ibn Dithar, Shurayh, and Mu'awiyah ibn Qurrah.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter of Testimony of the Slanderer, Thief, and Adulterer, no. 2648). Evidence: (3) The verse for establishing: 'And those who accuse chaste women and then do not produce four witnesses - flog them with eighty stripes and never accept their testimony ever after. And those are the defiantly disobedient, except for those who repent afterwards and reform; indeed Allah is Forgiving and Merciful.' (Surah al-Nur, 24:4-5). Principle: In transactions, the testimony of sinful persons is accepted, but in religious matters, the testimony of sinful persons is not accepted.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs concerning the acceptance of a fasiq's (sinful person's) testimony. The ruling is that in mu'amalat (transactions and civil matters), the testimony of a fasiq is accepted, but in akhbar al-diyanat (religious reports, such as hadith or testimony about religious matters), only an 'adl (just person) is accepted. The author then provides three evidences: (1) A verse from Surah al-Hajj (22:30) commanding avoidance of false speech, which implies that sinful speech is rejected in religious matters, but transactions are different. (2) The practice of Umar and other companions/early authorities showing that after a slanderer repents, his testimony is accepted in legal matters, indicating that in transactions, repentance suffices. (3) The verses from Surah al-Nur (24:4-5) which explicitly reject the testimony of those who slander without four witnesses, but make an exception for those who repent, implying that the original rejection applies to religious reports, not transactions. The Urdu principle summarizes: In transactions, the testimony of sinful persons is accepted, but in religious matters, it is not.

Key Terms
فاسق (fāsiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins without repentance.
معاملات (muʿāmalāt): Transactional matters such as trade, contracts, debts, and civil disputes.
ديانات (diyānāt): Religious matters such as hadith transmission, testimonies about creed, or reports related to worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which type of cases is a fasiq's testimony accepted according to this passage?
A) Religious matters
B) Transactions only
C) All cases
D) Criminal cases

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts a fasiq's testimony in transactional matters based on the Quranic exception for repentance and the practice of Umar, but rejects it in religious reports.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Judge and Witness May Look at Woman's Face
Exception for judge and witness to look at woman's face for judgment or testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a judge or witness looking at a woman's face for legal purposes and explain the basis in the hadith.

Core Idea
A judge and witness may look at a woman's face for judgment or testimony, overriding the general prohibition, even if desire is feared.

In Islamic law, looking at a non-mahram woman is generally prohibited. However, there are exceptions for necessity. This lesson explores the exception for judges and witnesses who need to see the woman's face to fulfill their duties. We will examine the explicit ruling in al-Quduri and its prophetic proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being permitted? Looking at a woman's face. Who is permitted? A judge when he intends to pass judgment, and a witness when he intends to testify. The ruling is permissibility (jawaz), even if desire is feared.
The ruling is mubah, not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Abu Hurayrah where the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded a man who had married an Ansari woman to go and look at her, saying 'there is something in the eyes of the Ansar.' This is an ahad hadith from Sahih Muslim.
Thubut is zanni, but dalala is qati because the command indicates permissibility.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's command to look at a woman for marriage (a need) indicates that looking for a necessity is permissible even if desire may arise. The judge and witness have a greater need (hajah) for identification and testimony, so by analogy (qiyas) they are allowed to look.
The analogy is strengthened by the fact that the judge's need is for justice, which is a higher purpose.
4
Note the absence of ikhtilaf
This ruling is agreed upon among the Hanafis and other schools. There is no significant intra-madhhab or inter-madhhab dispute on the permissibility for judge and witness.
The ruling is muttafaq alayh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ لِلْقَاضِي إِذَا أَرَادَ أَنْ يَحْكُمَ عَلَيْهَا وَلِلشَّاهِدِ إِذَا أَرَادَ أَنْ يَشْهَدَ عَلَيْهَا أَنْ يَنْظُرَ إِلَى وَجْهِهَا وَإِنْ خَافَ أَنْ يَشْتَهِيَ

وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ لِلْقَاضِي إِذَا أَرَادَ أَنْ يَحْكُمَ عَلَيْهَا \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ. قَالَ: كُنْتُ عند التي فَأَتَاهُ رَجُلٌ فَأَخْبَرَهُ أَنَّهُ تَزَوَّجَ امْرَأَةَ مِنَ الأَنْصَارِ. فَقَالَ لَهُ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : "أَنَظَرْتَ إِلَيْهَا؟ " قَالَ : لَا. قَالَ: "فَاذْهَبْ فَانْظُرْ إِلَيْهَا . فَإِنَّ فِي أَعْيُنِ الْأَنْصَارِ شَيْئًا»( مسلم شريف، بَاب نَدْبِ النَّظَرِ إِلَى وَجْهِ الْمَرْأَةِ وَكَفَّيْهَا لِمَنْ يُرِيدُ تَزَوُّجَهَا، غير 1424)
And it is permissible for the judge, when he intends to pass a judgment concerning her, and for the witness, when he intends to testify concerning her, to look at her face, even if he fears that he may desire. Evidence: (1) The hadith for establishing: from Abu Hurayrah who said: I was with the Prophet when a man came and informed him that he had married a woman from the Ansar. The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said to him: 'Did you look at her?' He said: No. He said: 'Go and look at her, for indeed there is something in the eyes of the Ansar.' (Sahih Muslim, Chapter on Recommending Looking at the Face and Hands of a Woman for One Who Wants to Marry Her, no. 1424).
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage is a ruling that permits a judge and a witness to look at the face of a woman when it is necessary for judgment or testimony, even if they fear desire. The proof is the hadith where the Prophet commanded a man who wanted to marry to look at the woman's face, which indicates that looking for a need is permissible even if desire is present. By analogy, a judge and a witness have a greater need.

Key Terms
قاض (qāḍī): A judge who needs to see the face of a woman to identify her or pass judgment.
شاهد (shāhid): A witness who needs to identify the woman for testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a judge who intends to pass a judgment on a woman?
A) He must avoid looking at her face
B) He may look at her face only if he does not fear desire
C) He may look at her face even if he fears desire
D) He cannot look at her face at all

Key Takeaway
Judges and witnesses are permitted to look at a woman's face for legal necessity, even if desire is feared, based on prophetic analogy.
